    Self::Negative => f.write_str(\\\"negative\\\"),\\n272:         }\\n273:     }\\n274: }\\n275: \\n276: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\\n277: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n278: #[cfg_attr(\\n279:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n280:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n281: )]\\n282: pub enum ExistentialPredicate<I: Interner> {\\n283:     /// E.g., `Iterator`.\\n284:     Trait(ExistentialTraitRef<I>),\\n285:     /// E.g., `Iterator::Item = T`.\\n286:     Projection(ExistentialProjection<I>),\\n287:     /// E.g., `Send`.\\n288:     AutoTrait(I::TraitId),\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialPredicate<I> {}\\n292: \\n293: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\\n294:     /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\\n295:     /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\\n296:     /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\\n297:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\\n302:             }\\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\\n306:                     ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\\n307:                 } else {\\n308:                     // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\\n309:                     // new error args for the missing generics.\\n310:                     let err_args =\\n311:                         GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\\n312:                     ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\\n313:                 };\\n314:                 self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\\n315:             }\\n316:         }\\n317:     }\\n318: }\\n319: \\n320: /// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\\n321: /// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\\n322: /// ```ignore (illustrative)\\n323: /// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\\n324: /// ```\\n325: /// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\\n326: /// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\\n327: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\\n328: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n329: #[cfg_attr(\\n330:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n331:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n332: )]\\n333: pub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\\n334:     pub def_id: I::TraitId,\\n335:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n336:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\\n337:     /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\\n338:     _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n339: }\\n340: \\n341: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\\n342: \\n343: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n344:     pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\\n345:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\\n346:         Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\\n347:     }\\n348: \\n349:     pub fn new(\\n350:         interner: I,\\n351:         trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\\n352:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n353:     ) -> Self {\\n354:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n355:         Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\\n356:     }\\n357: \\n358:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n359:         // Assert there is a Self.\\n360:         trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\\n361: \\n362:         ExistentialTraitRef {\\n363:             def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\\n364:             args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\\n365:             _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n366:         }\\n367:     }\\n368: \\n369:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\\n370:     /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\\n371:     /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\\n372:     /// or some placeholder type.\\n373:     pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\\n374:         // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\\n375:         // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\\n376: \\n377:         TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\\n378:     }\\n379: }\\n380: \\n381: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\\n382:     pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\\n383:         self.skip_binder().def_id\\n384:     }\\n385: \\n386:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. \\n293: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\\n294:     /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\\n295:     /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\\n296:     /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\\n297:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\\n302:             }\\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\\n306:                     ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\\n307:                 } else {\\n308:                     // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\\n309:                     // new error args for the missing generics.\\n310:                     let err_args =\\n311:                         GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\\n312:                     ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\\n313:                 };\\n314:                 self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\\n315:             }\\n316:         }\\n317:     }\\n318: }\\n319: \\n320: /// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\\n321: /// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\\n322: /// ```ignore (illustrative)\\n323: /// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\\n324: /// ```\\n325: /// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\\n326: /// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\\n327: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\\n328: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n329: #[cfg_attr(\\n330:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n331:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n332: )]\\n333: pub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\\n334:     pub def_id: I::TraitId,\\n335:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n336:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\\n337:     /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\\n338:     _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n339: }\\n340: \\n341: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\\n342: \\n343: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n344:     pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\\n345:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\\n346:         Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\\n347:     }\\n348: \\n349:     pub fn new(\\n350:         interner: I,\\n351:         trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\\n352:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n353:     ) -> Self {\\n354:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n355:         Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\\n356:     }\\n357: \\n358:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n359:         // Assert there is a Self.\\n360:         trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\\n361: \\n362:         ExistentialTraitRef {\\n363:             def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\\n364:             args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\\n365:             _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n366:         }\\n367:     }\\n368: \\n369:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\\n370:     /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\\n371:     /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\\n372:     /// or some placeholder type.\\n373:     pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\\n374:         // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\\n375:         // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\\n376: \\n377:         TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\\n378:     }\\n379: }\\n380: \\n381: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\\n382:     pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\\n383:         self.skip_binder().def_id\\n384:     }\\n385: \\n386:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. I: Interner)]\\n397: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n398: #[cfg_attr(\\n399:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n400:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n401: )]\\n402: pub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\\n403:     pub def_id: I::DefId,\\n404:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n405:     pub term: I::Term,\\n406: \\n407:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\\n408:     /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\\n409:     use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\\n410: }\\n411: \\n412: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\\n413: \\n414: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n415:     pub fn new_from_args(\\n416:         interner: I,\\n417:         def_id: I::DefId,\\n418:         args: I::GenericArgs,\\n419:         term: I::Term,\\n420:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n421:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\\n422:         Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\\n423:     }\\n424: \\n425:     pub fn new(\\n426:         interner: I,\\n427:         def_id: I::DefId,\\n428:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n429:         term: I::Term,\\n430:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n431:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n432:         Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\\n433:     }\\n434: \\n435:     /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\\n436:     /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\\n437:     /// then this function would return an `exists T.      let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\\n442:         let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\\n443: PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \\\"nightly\\\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\\n488:     ProjectionTy,\\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\\n490:     InherentTy,\\n491:     /// #[cfg_attr(\\n557:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n558:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n559: )]\\n560: pub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\\n561:     /// any.\\n565:     ///\\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\\n567:     /// if there are any.\\n568:     ///\\n569:     /// For RPIT the generic {\\n624:         interner.alias_term_kind(self)\\n625:     }\\n626: \\n627:     pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\\n628:         match self.kind(interner) {\\n629:            ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\\n638:                 ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\\n639:             )\\n640:       )\\n660:             .into(),\\n661:         }\\n662:     }\\n663: }\\n664: \\n665: /// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\\n666: impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\\n667:     pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\\n668:         self.args.type_at(0)\\n669:     }\\n670: \\n671:     pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self }\\n746: }\\n747: \\n748: impl<I: Interner> From<ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\\n749:     fn from(ct: ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>) -> Self {\\n750:         AliasTerm { args: ct.args, def_id: ct.def.into(), _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\\n751:     }\\n752: }\\n753: \\n754: /// This kind of predicate has no *direct* correspondent in the\\n755: /// syntax, but it roughly corresponds to the syntactic forms:\\n756: ///\\n757: /// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\\n758: /// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\\n759: ///\\n760: /// In particular, form #1 is \\\"desugared\\\" to the combination of a\\n761: /// normal trait predicate (`T: TraitRef<...>`) and one of these\\n762: /// predicates. Form #2 is a broader form in that it also permits\\n763: /// equality between arbitrary types. Processing an instance of\\n764: /// Form #2 eventually yields one of these `ProjectionPredicate`\\n765: /// instances to normalize the LHS.\\n766: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: \\n777: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ProjectionPredicate<I> {}\\n778: \\n779: impl<I: Interner> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\\n780:     pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\\n781: Projection(ExistentialProjection<I>),\n287:     /// E.g., `Send`.\n288:     AutoTrait(I::TraitId),\n289: }\n290: \n291: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialPredicate<I> {}\n292: \n293: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\n294:     /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\n295:     /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\n296:     /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\n297:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\n302:             }\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\n306:                     ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\n307:                 } else {\n308:                     // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\n309:                     // new error args for the missing generics.\n310:                     let err_args =\n311:                         GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\n312:                     ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\n313:                 };\n314:                 self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n315:             }\n316:         }\n317:     }\n318: }\n319: \n320: /// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n321: /// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n322: /// ```ignore (illustrative)\n323: /// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n324: /// ```\n325: /// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n326: /// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n327: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n328: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n329: #[cfg_attr(\n330:     feature = \"nightly\",\n331:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n332: )]\n333: pub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n334:     pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n335:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n336:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n337:     /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n338:     _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n339: }\n340: \n341: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n342: \n343: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n344:     pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n345:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n346:         Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n347:     }\n348: \n349:     pub fn new(\n350:         interner: I,\n351:         trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n352:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n353:     ) -> Self {\n354:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n355:         Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n356:     }\n357: \n358:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n359:         // Assert there is a Self.\n360:         trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n361: \n362:         ExistentialTraitRef {\n363:             def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n364:             args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n365:             _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n366:         }\n367:     }\n368: \n369:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n370:     /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n371:     /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n372:     /// or some placeholder type.\n373:     pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n374:         // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n375:         // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n376: \n377:         TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n378:     }\n379: }\n380: \n381: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n382:     pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n383:         self.skip_binder().def_id\n384:     }\n385: \n386:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n387:     /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n388:     /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n389:     /// or some placeholder type.\n390:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n391:         self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n392:     }\n393: }\n394: \n395: /// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n396: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n397: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n398: #[cfg_attr(\n399:     feature = \"nightly\",\n400:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n401: )]\n402: pub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n403:     pub def_id: I::DefId,\n404:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n405:     pub term: I::Term,\n406: \n407:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n408:     /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n409:     use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n410: }\n411: \n412: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n413: \n414: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n415:     pub fn new_from_args(\n416:         interner: I,\n417:         def_id: I::DefId,\n418:         args: I::GenericArgs,\n419:         term: I::Term,\n420:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n421:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n422:         Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n423:     }\n424: \n425:     pub fn new(\n426:         interner: I,\n427:         def_id: I::DefId,\n428:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n429:         term: I::Term,\n430:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n431:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n432:         Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n433:     }\n434: \n435:     /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n436:     /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n437:     /// then this function would return an `exists T.        interner,\n453:                 self.def_id,\n454:                 [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n455:             ),\n456:             term: self.term,\n457:         }\n458:     }\n459: \n460:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n461:         // Assert there is a Self.\n462:         projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n463: \n464:         Self {\n465:             def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n466:             args:     }\n470:     }\n471: }\n472: \n473: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n474:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n475:         self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n476:     }\n477: \n478:     pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n479:         self.skip_binder().def_id\n480:     }\n481: }\n482: \n483: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n488:     ProjectionTy,\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n490:     InherentTy,\n491:     /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n492:     /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n493:     OpaqueTy,\n494:     /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n495:     /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n496:     /// InherentConst,\n507: }\n508: \n509: impl AliasTermKind {\n510:     pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n511:         match self {\n512:             AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n513:             AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n514:             AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n515:             AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n516:             AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n517:             AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n518:             AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n519:             AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n520:         }\n521:     }\n522: \n523:     pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n524:         match self {\n525:             AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n526:             | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n527:             | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n528:             |      | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n534:         }\n535:     }\n536: }\n537: \n538: impl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n539:     fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n540:          ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n545:         }\n546:     }\n547: }\n548: \n549: /// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n550: ///\n551: /// * For a projection, ///\n563:     /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n564:     /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n565:     ///\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they /// The following methods work only with inherent associated term projections.\n718: impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n719:     /// Transform the generic parameters to have the given `impl` args as }\n747: \n748: impl<I: Interner> From<ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n749:     fn from(ct: ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>) -> Self {\n750:         AliasTerm { args: ct.args, def_id: ct.def.into(), _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n751:     }\n752: }\n753: \n754: /// This kind of predicate has no *direct* correspondent in the\n755: /// syntax, but it roughly corresponds to the syntactic forms:\n756: ///\n757: /// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\n758: /// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\n759: ///\n760: /// In particular, form #1 is \"desugared\" to the combination of a\n761: /// normal trait predicate (`T: TraitRef<...>`) and one of these\n762: /// predicates. Form #2 is a broader form in that it also permits\n763: /// equality between arbitrary types. Processing an instance of\n764: /// Form #2 eventually yields one of these `ProjectionPredicate`\n765: /// instances to normalize the LHS.\n766: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n767: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n768: #[cfg_attr(\n769:     feature = \"nightly\",\n770:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n771: )]\n772: pub struct ProjectionPredicate<I: Interner> {\n773:     pub projection_term: AliasTerm<I>,\n774:     pub term: I::Term,\n775: }\n776: \n777: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ProjectionPredicate<I> {}\n778: \n779: impl<I: Interner> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n780:     pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n781:         self.projection_term.self_ty()\n782:     }\n783: \n784: ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n801:     /// Returns the `DefId` of the trait of the associated item being projected.\n802:     #[inline]\n803:     pub fn trait_def_id(&self, cx: I) -> self.projection_bounds()\\n288:     }\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: impl<'tcx> ty::List<ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\\n292:     /// Returns the \\\"principal `DefId`\\\" of this set of existential predicates.\\n293:     ///\\n294:     /// A Rust trait object type consists (in addition to a lifetime bound)\\n295:     /// of a set of trait bounds, which are separated into any number\\n296:     /// of auto-trait bounds, and at most one non-auto-trait bound. The\\n297:     /// non-auto-trait bound is called the \\\"principal\\\" of the trait\\n298:     /// object.\\n299:     ///\\n300:     /// Only the principal can have methods or type parameters (because\\n301:     /// auto traits can have neither of them). This is important, because\\n302:     /// it means the auto traits can be treated as an unordered set (methods\\n303:     /// would force an order for the vtable, while relating traits with\\n304:     /// type parameters without knowing the order to relate them in is\\n305:     /// a rather non-trivial task).\\n306:     ///\\n307:     /// For example, in the trait object `dyn std::fmt::Debug + Sync`, the\\n308:     /// principal bound is `Some(std::fmt::Debug)`, while the auto-trait bounds\\n309:     /// are the set `{Sync}`.\\n310:     ///\\n311:     /// It is also possible to have a \\\"trivial\\\" trait object that\\n312:     /// consists only of auto traits, with no principal - for example,\\n313:     /// `dyn Send + Sync`. In that case, the set of auto-trait bounds\\n314:     /// is `{Send, Sync}`, while there is no principal. These trait objects\\n315:     /// have a \\\"trivial\\\" vtable consisting of just the size, alignment,\\n316:     /// and destructor.\\n317:     pub fn principal(&self) -> Option<ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>> {\\n318:         self[0]\\n319:             .map_bound(|this| match this {\\n320:                 ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => Some(tr),\\n321:                 _ => None,\\n322:             })\\n323:             .transpose()\\n324:     }\\n325: \\n326:     pub fn principal_def_id(&self) -> Option<DefId> {\\n327:         self.principal().map(|trait_ref| }\\n343: \\n344:     #[inline]\\n345:     pub fn auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = DefId> {\\n346:         self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| match predicate.skip_binder() {\\n347:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => Some(did),\\n348:             _ => None,\\n349:         })\\n350:     }\\n351: \\n352:     pub fn without_auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\\n353:         self.iter().filter(|predicate| {\\n354:             !matches!(predicate.as_ref().skip_binder(), ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(_))\\n355:         })\\n356:     }\\n357: }\\n358: \\n359: pub type PolyTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, TraitRef<'tcx>>;\\n360: pub type PolyExistentialTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>;\\n361: pub type PolyExistentialProjection<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>;\\n362: \\n363: impl<'tcx> Clause<'tcx> {\\n364:     /// Performs a instantiation suitable for going from a\\n365:     /// poly-trait-ref to supertraits that must hold if that\\n366:     /// poly-trait-ref holds. This is slightly different from a normal\\n367:     /// instantiation in terms of what happens with bound regions. See\\n368:     /// lengthy comment below for details.\\n369:     pub fn instantiate_supertrait(\\n370:         self,\\n371:         tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n372:         trait_ref: ty::PolyTraitRef<'tcx>,\\n373:     ) -> Clause<'tcx> {\\n374:         // The interaction between HRTB and supertraits is not entirely\\n375:         // obvious. Let me walk you (and myself) through an example.\\n376:         //\\n377:         // Let's start with an easy case. Consider two traits:\\n378:         //\\n379:         //     trait Foo<'a>: Bar<'a,'a> { }\\n380:         //     trait Bar<'b,'c> { }\\n381:         //\\n382:         // Now, if we have a trait reference `for<'x> T: Foo<'x>`, then\\n383:         // we can deduce that `for<'x> T: Bar<'x,'x>`. Basically, if we\\n384:         // knew that `Foo<'x>` (for any 'x) then we also know that\\n385:         // `Bar<'x,'x>` (for any 'x). This more-or-less falls out from\\n386:         // normal instantiation.\\n387:         //\\n388:         // In terms of why this is sound, the idea is that whenever there\\n389:         // is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>`, it must show that `T:Bar<'a,'a>`\\n390:         // holds. So if there is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>` that applies to\\n391:         // all `'a`, then we must know that `T:Bar<'a,'a>` holds for all\\n392:         // `'a`.\\n393:         //\\n394:         // Another example to be careful of is this:\\n395:         //\\n396:         //     trait Foo1<'a>: for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b> { }\\n397:         //     trait Bar1<'b,'c> { }\\n398:         //\\n399:         // Here, if we have `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`, then what do we know?\\n400:         // The answer is that we know `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`. The\\n401:         // reason is similar to the previous example: any impl of\\n402:         // `T:Foo1<'x>` must show that `for<'b> T: Bar1<'x, 'b>`. So\\n403:         // basically we would want to collapse the bound lifetimes from\\n404:         // the input (`trait_ref`) and the supertraits.\\n405:         //\\n406:         // To achieve this in practice is fairly straightforward. Let's\\n407:         // consider the more complicated scenario:\\n408:         //\\n409:         // - We start out with `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`. In this case, `'x`\\n410:         //   has a De Bruijn index of 1. We want to produce `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`,\\n411:         //   where both `'x` and `'b` would have a DB index of 1.\\n412:         //   The instantiation from the input trait-ref is therefore going to be\\n413:         //   `'a => 'x` (where `'x` has a DB index of 1).\\n414:         // - The supertrait-ref is `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, where `'a` is an\\n415:         //   early-bound parameter and `'b` is a late-bound parameter with a\\n416:         //   DB index of 1.\\n417:         // - If we replace `'a` with `'x` from the input, it too will have\\n418:         //   a DB index of 1, and thus we'll have `for<'x,'b> Bar1<'x,'b>`\\n419:         //   just as we wanted.\\n420:         //\\n421:         // There is only one catch. If we just apply the instantiation `'a\\n422:         // => 'x` to `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, the instantiation code will\\n423:         // adjust the DB index because we instantiating into a binder (it\\n424:         // tries to be so smart...) resulting in `for<'x> for<'b>\\n425:         // Bar1<'x,'b>` (we have no syntax for this, so use your\\n426:         // imagination). Basically the 'x will have DB index of 2 and 'b\\n427:         // will have DB index of 1. Not quite what we want. So we apply\\n428:         // the instantiation to the *contents* of the trait reference,\\n429:         // rather than the trait reference itself (put another way, the\\n430:         // instantiation code expects equal binding levels in the values\\n431:         // from the instantiation and the value being instantiated into, and\\n432:         // this trick achieves that).\\n433: \\n434:         // Working through the second example:\\n435:         // trait_ref: for<'x> T: Foo1<'^0.0>; args: [T, '^0.0]\\n436:         // predicate: for<'b> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0>; args: [Self, 'a, '^0.0]\\n437:         // We want to end up with:\\n438:         //     for<'x, 'b> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\\n439:         // To do this:\\n440:         // 1) We must shift all bound vars in predicate by the length\\n441:         //    of trait ref's bound vars. So, we would end up with predicate like\\n442:         //    Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\\n443:         // 2) We can then apply the trait args to this, ending up with\\n444:         //    T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\\n445:         // 3) Finally, to create the final bound vars, we concatenate the bound\\n446:         //    vars of the trait ref with those of the predicate:\\n447:         //    ['x, 'b]\\n448:         let bound_pred = self.kind();\\n449:         let pred_bound_vars = bound_pred.bound_vars();\\n450:         let trait_bound_vars = trait_ref.bound_vars();\\n451:         // 1) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0> -> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\\n452:         let shifted_pred =\\n453:             tcx.shift_bound_var_indices(trait_bound_vars.len(), bound_pred.skip_binder());\\n454:         // 2) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1> -> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\\n455:         let new = EarlyBinder::bind(shifted_pred).instantiate(tcx, trait_ref.skip_binder().args);\\n456:         // 3) ['x] + ['b] -> ['x, 'b]\\n457:         let bound_vars =\\n458:             tcx.mk_bound_variable_kinds_from_iter(trait_bound_vars.iter().chain(pred_bound_vars));\\n459: \\n460:         // FIXME: Is it really perf sensitive to use reuse_or_mk_predicate here?\\n461:         tcx.reuse_or_mk_predicate(\\n462:             self.as_predicate(),\\n463:             ty::Binder::bind_with_vars(PredicateKind::Clause(new), bound_vars),\\n464:         )\\n465:         .expect_clause()\\n466:     }\\n467: }\\n468: \\n469: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, PredicateKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\\n470:     fn upcast_from(from: PredicateKind<'tcx>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\\n471:         ty::Binder::dummy(from).upcast(tcx)\\n472:     }\\n473: }\\n474: \\n475: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty::Binder<'tcx, PredicateKind<'tcx>>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\\n476:     fn upcast_from(from: ty::Binder<'tcx, PredicateKind<'tcx>>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\\n477:         tcx.mk_predicate(from)\\n478:     }\\n479: }\\n480: \\n481: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ClauseKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\\n482:     fn upcast_from(from: ClauseKind<'tcx>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\\n483:         tcx.mk_predicate(ty::Binder::dummy(PredicateKind::Clause(from)))\\n484:     }\\n485: }\\n486: \\n487: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty::Binder<'tcx, \\n242: impl<'tcx> rustc_type_ir::inherent::Clauses<TyCtxt<'tcx>> for ty::Clauses<'tcx> {}\\n243: \\n244: #[extension(pub trait ExistentialPredicateStableCmpExt<'tcx>)]\\n245: impl<'tcx> ExistentialPredicate<'tcx> {\\n246:     /// Compares via an ordering that will not change if modules are reordered or other changes are\\n247:     /// made to the tree. In particular, this ordering is preserved across incremental compilations.\\n248:     fn stable_cmp(&self, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, other: &Self) -> Ordering {\\n249:         match (*self, *other) {\\n250:             (ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_), ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_)) => Ordering::Equal,\\n251:             (ExistentialPredicate::Projection(ref a), ExistentialPredicate::Projection(ref b)) => self.projection_bounds()\\n288:     }\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: impl<'tcx> ty::List<ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\\n292:     /// Returns the \\\"principal `DefId`\\\" of this set of existential predicates.\\n293:     ///\\n294:     /// A Rust trait object type consists (in addition to a lifetime bound)\\n295:     /// of a set of trait bounds, which are separated into any number\\n296:     /// of auto-trait bounds, and at most one non-auto-trait bound. The\\n297:     /// non-auto-trait bound is called the \\\"principal\\\" of the trait\\n298:     /// object.\\n299:     ///\\n300:     /// Only the principal can have methods or type parameters (because\\n301:     /// auto traits can have neither of them). This is important, because\\n302:     /// it means the auto traits can be treated as an unordered set (methods\\n303:     /// would force an order for the vtable, while relating traits with\\n304:     /// type parameters without knowing the order to relate them in is\\n305:     /// a rather non-trivial task).\\n306:     ///\\n307:     /// For example, in the trait object `dyn std::fmt::Debug + Sync`, the\\n308:     /// principal bound is `Some(std::fmt::Debug)`, while the auto-trait bounds\\n309:     /// are the set `{Sync}`.\\n310:     ///\\n311:     /// It is also possible to have a \\\"trivial\\\" trait object that\\n312:     /// consists only of auto traits, with no principal - for example,\\n313:     /// `dyn Send + Sync`. In that case, the set of auto-trait bounds\\n314:     /// is `{Send, Sync}`, while there is no principal. These trait objects\\n315:     /// have a \\\"trivial\\\" vtable consisting of just the size, alignment,\\n316:     /// and destructor.\\n317:     pub fn principal(&self) -> Option<ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>> {\\n318:         self[0]\\n319:             .map_bound(|this| match this {\\n320:                 ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => Some(tr),\\n321:                 _ => None,\\n322:             })\\n323:             .transpose()\\n324:     }\\n325: \\n326:     pub fn principal_def_id(&self) -> Option<DefId> {\\n327:         self.principal().map(|trait_ref| trait_ref.skip_binder().def_id)\\n328:     }\\n329: \\n330:     #[inline]\\n331:     pub fn projection_bounds(\\n332:         &self,\\n333:     ) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>> {\\n334:         self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| {\\n335:             predicate\\n336:                 .map_bound(|pred| match pred {\\n337:                     ExistentialPredicate::Projection(projection) => Some(projection),\\n338:                     _ => None,\\n339:                 })\\n340:                 .transpose()\\n341:         })\\n342:     }\\n343: \\n344:     #[inline]\\n345:     pub fn auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = DefId> {\\n346:         self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| match predicate.skip_binder() {\\n347: })\\n356:     }\\n357: }\\n358: \\n359: pub type PolyTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, TraitRef<'tcx>>;\\n360: pub type PolyExistentialTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>;\\n361: pub type PolyExistentialProjection<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>;\\n362: \\n363: impl<'tcx> Clause<'tcx> {\\n364:     /// Performs a instantiation suitable for going from a\\n365:     /// poly-trait-ref to supertraits that must hold if that\\n366:     /// poly-trait-ref holds. This is slightly different from a normal\\n367:     /// instantiation in terms of what happens with bound regions. See\\n368:     /// lengthy comment below for details.\\n369:     pub fn instantiate_supertrait(\\n370:         self,\\n371:         tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n372:         trait_ref: ty::PolyTraitRef<'tcx>,\\n373:     ) -> Clause<'tcx> {\\n374:         // The interaction between HRTB and supertraits is not entirely\\n375:         // obvious. Let me walk you (and myself) through an example.\\n376:         //\\n377:         // Let's start with an easy case. Consider two traits:\\n378:         //\\n379:         //     trait Foo<'a>: Bar<'a,'a> { }\\n380:         //     trait Bar<'b,'c> { }\\n381:         //\\n382:         // Now, if we have a trait reference `for<'x> T: Foo<'x>`, then\\n383:         // we can deduce that `for<'x> T: Bar<'x,'x>`. Basically, if we\\n384:         // knew that `Foo<'x>` (for any 'x) then we also know that\\n385:         // `Bar<'x,'x>` (for any 'x). This more-or-less falls out from\\n386:         // normal instantiation.\\n387:         //\\n388:         // In terms of why this is sound, the idea is that whenever there\\n389:         // is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>`, it must show that `T:Bar<'a,'a>`\\n390:         // holds. So if there is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>` that applies to\\n391:         // all `'a`, then we must know that `T:Bar<'a,'a>` holds for all\\n392:         // `'a`.\\n393:         //\\n394:         // Another example to be careful of is this:\\n395:         //\\n396:         //     trait Foo1<'a>: for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b> { }\\n397:         //     trait Bar1<'b,'c> { }\\n398:         //\\n399:         // Here, if we have `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`, then what do we know?\\n400:         // The answer is that we know `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`. The\\n401:         // reason is similar to the previous example: any impl of\\n402:         // `T:Foo1<'x>` must show that `for<'b> T: Bar1<'x, 'b>`. So\\n403:         // basically we would want to collapse the bound lifetimes from\\n404:         // the input (`trait_ref`) and the supertraits.\\n405:         //\\n406:         // To achieve this in practice is fairly straightforward. Let's\\n407:         // consider the more complicated scenario:\\n408:         //\\n409:         // - We start out with `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`. In this case, `'x`\\n410:         //   has a De Bruijn index of 1. We want to produce `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`,\\n411:         //   where both `'x` and `'b` would have a DB index of 1.\\n412:         //   The instantiation from the input trait-ref is therefore going to be\\n413:         //   `'a => 'x` (where `'x` has a DB index of 1).\\n414:         // - The supertrait-ref is `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, where `'a` is an\\n415:         //   early-bound parameter and `'b` is a late-bound parameter with a\\n416:         //   DB index of 1.\\n417:         // - If we replace `'a` with `'x` from the input, it too will have\\n418:         //   a DB index of 1, and thus we'll have `for<'x,'b> Bar1<'x,'b>`\\n419:         //   just as we wanted.\\n420:         //\\n421:         // There is only one catch. If we just apply the instantiation `'a\\n422:         // => 'x` to `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, the instantiation code will\\n423:         // adjust the DB index because we instantiating into a binder (it\\n424:         // tries to be so smart...) resulting in `for<'x> for<'b>\\n425:         // Bar1<'x,'b>` (we have no syntax for this, so use your\\n426:         // imagination). Basically the 'x will have DB index of 2 and 'b\\n427:         // will have DB index of 1. Not quite what we want. So we apply\\n428:         // the instantiation to the *contents* of the trait reference,\\n429:         // rather than the trait reference itself (put another way, the\\n430:         // instantiation code expects equal binding levels in the values\\n431:         // from the instantiation and the value being instantiated into, and\\n432:         // this trick achieves that).\\n433: \\n434:         // Working through the second example:\\n435:         // trait_ref: for<'x> T: Foo1<'^0.0>; args: [T, '^0.0]\\n436:         // predicate: for<'b> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0>; args: [Self, 'a, '^0.0]\\n437:         // We want to end up with:\\n438:         //     for<'x, 'b> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\\n439:         // To do this:\\n440:         // 1) We must shift all bound vars in predicate by the length\\n441:         //    of trait ref's bound vars. So, we would end up with predicate like\\n442:         //    Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\\n443:         // 2) We can then apply the trait args to this, ending up with\\n444:         //    T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\\n445:         // 3) Finally, to create the final bound vars, we concatenate the bound\\n446:         //    vars of the trait ref with those of the predicate:\\n447:         //    ['x, 'b]\\n448:         let bound_pred = self.kind();\\n449:         let pred_bound_vars = bound_pred.bound_vars();\\n450:         let trait_bound_vars = trait_ref.bound_vars();\\n451:         // 1) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0> -> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\\n452:         let shifted_pred =\\n453:             tcx.shift_bound_var_indices(trait_bound_vars.len(), bound_pred.skip_binder());\\n454:         // 2) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1> -> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\\n455:         let new = EarlyBinder::bind(shifted_pred).instantiate(tcx, trait_ref.skip_binder().args);\\n456:         // 3) ['x] + ['b] -> ['x, 'b]\\n457:         let bound_vars =\\n458:             tcx.mk_bound_variable_kinds_from_iter(trait_bound_vars.iter().chain(pred_bound_vars));\\n459: \\n460:         // FIXME: Is it really perf sensitive to use reuse_or_mk_predicate here?\\n461:         tcx.reuse_or_mk_predicate(\\n462:             self.as_predicate(),\\n463:             ty::Binder::bind_with_vars(PredicateKind::Clause(new), bound_vars),\\n464:         )\\n465:         .expect_clause()\\n466:     }\\n467: }\\n468: \\n469: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, PredicateKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\\n470:     fn upcast_from(from: PredicateKind<'tcx>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\\n471:         ty::Binder::dummy(from).upcast(tcx)\\n472:     }\\n473: }\\n474: \\n475: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, tcx.mk_predicate(from)\\n478:     }\\n479: }\\n480: \\n481: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ClauseKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\\n482:     fn upcast_from(from: ClauseKind<'tcx>, tcx: change if modules are reordered or other changes are\n247:     /// made to the tree. In particular, this ordering is preserved across incremental compilations.\n248:     fn stable_cmp(&self, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, other: &Self) -> Ordering {\n249:         match (*self, *other) {\n250:             (ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_), ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_)) => Ordering::Equal,\n251:             (ExistentialPredicate::Projection(ref a), ExistentialPredicate::Projection(ref b)) => Rust trait object type consists (in addition to a lifetime bound)\n295:     /// of a set of trait bounds, which are separated into any number\n296:     /// of auto-trait bounds, and at most one non-auto-trait bound. The\n297:     /// non-auto-trait bound is called the \"principal\" of the trait\n298:     /// object.\n299:     ///\n300:     /// Only the principal can have methods or type parameters (because\n301:     /// auto traits can have neither of them). This is important, because\n302:     /// it means the auto traits can be treated as an unordered set (methods\n303:     /// would force an order for the vtable, while relating traits with\n304:     /// type parameters without knowing the order to relate them in is\n305:     /// a rather non-trivial task).\n306:     ///\n307:     /// For example, in the trait object `dyn std::fmt::Debug + Sync`, the\n308:     /// principal bound is `Some(std::fmt::Debug)`, while the auto-trait bounds\n309:     /// are the set `{Sync}`.\n310:     ///\n311:     /// It is also possible to have a \"trivial\" trait object that\n312:     /// consists only of auto traits, with no principal - for example,\n313:     /// `dyn Send + Sync`. In that case, the set of auto-trait bounds\n314:     /// is `{Send, Sync}`, while there is no principal. These trait objects\n315:     /// have a \"trivial\" vtable consisting of just the size, alignment,\n316:     /// and destructor.\n317:     pub fn principal(&self) -> Option<ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>> {\n318:         self[0]\n319:             .map_bound(|this| match this {\n320:                 ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => Some(tr),\n321:                 _ => None,\n322:             })\n323:             .transpose()\n324:     }\n325: \n326:     pub fn principal_def_id(&self) -> Option<DefId> {\n327:         self.principal().map(|trait_ref| trait_ref.skip_binder().def_id)\n328:     }\n329: \n330:     #[inline]\n331:     pub fn projection_bounds(\n332:         &self,\n333:     ) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>> {\n334:         self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| {\n335:             predicate\n336:                 .map_bound(|pred| match pred {\n337:                     ExistentialPredicate::Projection(projection) => Some(projection),\n338:                     _ => None,\n339:                 })\n340:                 .transpose()\n341:         })\n342:     }\n343: \n344:     #[inline]\n345:     pub fn auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = DefId> {\n346:         self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| match predicate.skip_binder() {\n347:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => Some(did),\n348:             _ => None,\n349:         })\n350:     }\n351: \n352:     pub fn without_auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\n353:         self.iter().filter(|predicate| {\n354:             !matches!(predicate.as_ref().skip_binder(), ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(_))\n355:         })\n356:     }\n357: }\n358: \n359: pub type PolyTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, TraitRef<'tcx>>;\n360: pub type PolyExistentialTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>;\n361: pub type PolyExistentialProjection<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>;\n362: \n363: impl<'tcx> Clause<'tcx> {\n364:     /// Performs a instantiation suitable for going from a\n365:     /// poly-trait-ref to supertraits that must hold if that\n366:     /// poly-trait-ref holds. This is slightly different from a normal\n367:     /// instantiation in terms of what happens with bound regions. See\n368:     /// lengthy comment below for details.\n369:     pub fn instantiate_supertrait(\n370:         self,\n371:         tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n372:         trait_ref: ty::PolyTraitRef<'tcx>,\n373:     ) -> Clause<'tcx> {\n374:         // The interaction between HRTB and supertraits is not entirely\n375:         // obvious. Let me walk you (and myself) through an example.\n376:         //\n377:         // Let's start with an easy case. Consider two traits:\n378:         //\n379:         //     trait Foo<'a>: Bar<'a,'a> { }\n380:         //     trait Bar<'b,'c> { }\n381:         //\n382:         // Now, if we have a trait reference `for<'x> T: Foo<'x>`, then\n383:         // we can deduce that `for<'x> T: Bar<'x,'x>`. Basically, if we\n384:         // knew that `Foo<'x>` (for any 'x) then we also know that\n385:         // `Bar<'x,'x>` (for any 'x). This more-or-less falls out from\n386:         // normal instantiation.\n387:         //\n388:         // In terms of why this is sound, the idea is that whenever there\n389:         // is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>`, it must show that `T:Bar<'a,'a>`\n390:         // holds. So if there is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>` that applies to\n391:         // all `'a`, then we must know that `T:Bar<'a,'a>` holds for all\n392:         // `'a`.\n393:         //\n394:         // Another example to be careful of is this:\n395:         //\n396:         //     trait Foo1<'a>: for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b> { }\n397:         //     trait Bar1<'b,'c> { }\n398:         //\n399:         // Here, if we have `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`, then what do we know?\n400:         // The answer is that we know `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`. The\n401:         // reason is similar to the previous example: any impl of\n402:         // `T:Foo1<'x>` must show that `for<'b> T: Bar1<'x, 'b>`. So\n403:         // basically we would want to collapse the bound lifetimes from\n404:         // the input (`trait_ref`) and the supertraits.\n405:         //\n406:         // To achieve this in practice is fairly straightforward. Let's\n407:         // consider the more complicated scenario:\n408:         //\n409:         // - We start out with `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`. In this case, `'x`\n410:         //   has a De Bruijn index of 1. We want to produce `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`,\n411:         //   where both `'x` and `'b` would have a DB index of 1.\n412:         //   The instantiation from the input trait-ref is therefore going to be\n413:         //   `'a => 'x` (where `'x` has a DB index of 1).\n414:         // - The supertrait-ref is `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, where `'a` is an\n415:         //   early-bound parameter and `'b` is a late-bound parameter with a\n416:         //   DB index of 1.\n417:         // - If we replace `'a` with `'x` from the input, it too will have\n418:         //   a DB index of 1, and thus we'll have `for<'x,'b> Bar1<'x,'b>`\n419:         //   just as we wanted.\n420:         //\n421:         // There is only one catch. If we just apply the instantiation `'a\n422:         // => 'x` to `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, the instantiation code will\n423:         // adjust the DB index because we instantiating into a binder (it\n424:         // tries to be so smart...) resulting in `for<'x> for<'b>\n425:         // Bar1<'x,'b>` (we have no syntax for this, so use your\n426:         // imagination). Basically the 'x will have DB index of 2 and 'b\n427:         // will have DB index of 1. Not quite what we want. So we apply\n428:         // the instantiation to the *contents* of the trait reference,\n429:         // rather than the trait reference itself (put another way, the\n430:         // instantiation code expects equal binding levels in the values\n431:         // from the instantiation and the value being instantiated into, and\n432:         // this trick achieves that).\n433: \n434:         // Working through the second example:\n435:         // trait_ref: for<'x> T: Foo1<'^0.0>; args: [T, '^0.0]\n436:         // predicate: for<'b> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0>; args: [Self, 'a, '^0.0]\n437:         // We want to end up with:\n438:         //     for<'x, 'b> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n439:         // To do this:\n440:         // 1) We must shift all bound vars in predicate by the length\n441:         //    of trait ref's bound vars. So, we would end up with predicate like\n442:         //    Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\n443:         // 2) We can then apply the trait args to this, ending up with\n444:         //    T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n445:         // 3) Finally, to create the final bound vars, we concatenate the bound\n446:         //    vars of the trait ref with those of the predicate:\n447:         //    ['x, 'b]\n448:         let bound_pred = self.kind();\n449:         let pred_bound_vars = bound_pred.bound_vars();\n450:         let trait_bound_vars = trait_ref.bound_vars();\n451:         // 1) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0> -> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\n452:         let shifted_pred =\n453:             tcx.shift_bound_var_indices(trait_bound_vars.len(), bound_pred.skip_binder());\n454:         // 2) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1> -> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n455:         let new = EarlyBinder::bind(shifted_pred).instantiate(tcx, trait_ref.skip_binder().args);\n456:         // 3) ['x] + ['b] -> ['x, 'b]\n457:         let bound_vars =\n458:             tcx.mk_bound_variable_kinds_from_iter(trait_bound_vars.iter().chain(pred_bound_vars));\n459: \n460:         // FIXME: Is it really perf sensitive to use reuse_or_mk_predicate here?\n461:         tcx.reuse_or_mk_predicate(\n462:             self.as_predicate(),\n463:             ty::Binder::bind_with_vars(PredicateKind::Clause(new), bound_vars),\n464:         )\n465:         .expect_clause()\n466:     }\n467: }\n468: \n469: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, PredicateKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\n470:     fn upcast_from(from: PredicateKind<'tcx>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\n471:         ty::Binder::dummy(from).upcast(tcx)\n472:     }\n473: }\n474: \n475: impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty::Binder<'tcx, PredicateKind<'tcx>>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\n476: Positive,\n    /// `impl !Trait for Type`\n    Negative,\n    /// `#[rustc_reservation_impl] impl Trait for Type`\n    ///\n    /// This is a \"stability hack\", not a real Rust feature.\n    /// See /// The polarity marker in front of the impl trait ref if applicable.\n    pub fn as_str(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => \"\",\n            Self::Negative May either be negative or positive.\n/// Distinguished from [`ImplPolarity`] since we never compute goals with\n/// \"reservation\" level.\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash,  /// `Type: !Trait`\n    Negative,\n}\n\nimpl PredicatePolarity {\n    /// Flips polarity by turning `Positive` into `Negative` and `Negative` into `Positive`.\n    pub fn flip(&self) -> PredicatePolarity {\n        match self {\n            PredicatePolarity::Positive => PredicatePolarity::Negative,\n            PredicatePolarity::Negative => PredicatePolarity::Positive,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for PredicatePolarity {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => f.write_str(\"positive\"),\n            Self::Negative => f.write_str(\"negative\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum ExistentialPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    /// E.g., `Iterator`.\n    Trait(ExistentialTraitRef<I>),\n    /// E.g., `Iterator::Item = T`.\n    Projection(ExistentialProjection<I>),\n    /// E.g., `Send`.\n    AutoTrait(I::TraitId),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\n    /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\n    /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\n    /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n        match self.skip_binder() {\n            ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\n            ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\n                self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\n            }\n            ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\n                let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\n                let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\n                    ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\n                } else {\n                    // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\n                    // new error args for the missing generics.\n                    let err_args =\n                        GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\n                    ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\n                };\n                self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n/// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n/// ```ignore (illustrative)\n/// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n/// ```\n/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n\n        ExistentialTraitRef {\n            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: I::GenericArgs,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n    /// then this function would return an `exists T. args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        ProjectionPredicate {\n            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n                interner,\n                self.def_id,\n                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n            ),\n            term: self.term,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n\n        Self {\n            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            term: projection_predicate.term,\n            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\npub enum AliasTermKind {\n    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n    ProjectionTy,\n    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentTy,\n    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n    OpaqueTy,\n    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n    /// Can always be normalized away.\n    FreeTy,\n\n    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n    UnevaluatedConst,\n    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n    ProjectionConst,\n    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n    FreeConst,\n    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentConst,\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind {\n    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n///\n/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n/// * For an opaque type, there is no Some((expected, found))\n        } else {\n            None\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The trace designates the path through inference that we took to\n/// encounter an error or subtyping    },\n\n    AscribeUserTypeProvePredicate(Span),\n}\n\n// `SubregionOrigin` is used a lot. Make sure it doesn't unintentionally get bigger.\n#[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\nrustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(SubregionOrigin<'_>, 32);\n\nimpl<'tcx> SubregionOrigin<'tcx> {\n    pub fn to_constraint_category(&self) -> ConstraintCategory<'tcx> {\n        match self {\n            Self::Subtype(type_trace) => type_trace.cause.to_constraint_category(),\n            Self::AscribeUserTypeProvePredicate(span) => ConstraintCategory::Predicate(*span),\n            _ => ConstraintCategory::BoringNoLocation,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Times when we replace bound regions with existentials:\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug)]\npub enum BoundRegionConversionTime {\n    /// when a fn is called\n    FnCall,\n\n    /// when two higher-ranked types are compared\n    HigherRankedType,\n\n    /// when projecting an associated type\n    AssocTypeProjection(DefId),\n}\n\n/// Reasons to create a region inference variable.\n///\n/// See `error_reporting` module for refactoring.\n    Misc(Span),\n\n    /// Regions created by a `&P` or `[...]` pattern.\n    PatternRegion(Span),\n\n    /// Regions created by `&` operator.\n    BorrowRegion(Span),\n\n    /// Regions
