 unresolved: TyOrConstInferVar,\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for FixupError {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        match self.unresolved {\n            TyOrConstInferVar::TyInt(_) => write!(\n                f,\n                \"cannot determine the type of this integer; \\\n                 add a suffix to specify the type explicitly\"\n            ),\n            TyOrConstInferVar::TyFloat(_) => write!(\n                f,\n                \"cannot determine the type of this number; \\\n                 add a suffix to specify the type explicitly\"\n            ),\n            TyOrConstInferVar::Ty(_) => write!(f, \"unconstrained type\"),\n            TyOrConstInferVar::Const(_) => write!(f, \"unconstrained const value\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// See the `region_obligations` field for more information.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug)]\npub struct TypeOutlivesConstraint<'tcx> {\n    pub sub_region: ty::Region<'tcx>,\n    pub sup_type: Ty<'tcx>,\n    pub origin: SubregionOrigin<'tcx>,\n}\n\n/// Used to configure inference contexts before their creation.\npub struct InferCtxtBuilder<'tcx> {\n    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n    considering_regions: bool,\n    in_hir_typeck: bool,\n    skip_leak_check: bool,\n    /// Whether we should use the new trait solver in the local inference context,\n    /// which affects things like which solver is used in `predicate_may_hold`.\n    next_trait_solver: bool,\n}\n\n#[extension(pub trait TyCtxtInferExt<'tcx>)]\nimpl<'tcx> TyCtxt<'tcx> {\n    fn infer_ctxt(self) -> InferCtxtBuilder<'tcx> {\n        InferCtxtBuilder {\n            tcx: self,\n            considering_regions: true,\n            in_hir_typeck: false,\n            skip_leak_check: false,\n            next_trait_solver: self.next_trait_solver_globally(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> InferCtxtBuilder<'tcx> {\n    pub fn with_next_trait_solver(mut self, next_trait_solver: bool) -> Self {\n        self.next_trait_solver = next_trait_solver;\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn ignoring_regions(mut self) -> Self {\n        self.considering_regions = false;\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn in_hir_typeck(mut self) -> Self {\n        self.in_hir_typeck = true;\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn skip_leak_check(mut self, skip_leak_check: bool) -> Self {\n        self.skip_leak_check = skip_leak_check;\n        self\n    }\n\n    /// Given a canonical value `C` as a starting point, create an\n    /// inference context that contains each of the bound values\n    /// within instantiated as a fresh variable. The `f` closure is\n    /// invoked with the new infcx, along with the instantiated value\n    /// `V` and a instantiation `S`. This instantiation `S` maps from\n    /// the bound values in `C` to their instantiated values in `V`\n    /// (in other words, `S(C) = V`).\n    pub fn build_with_canonical<T>(\n        mut self,\n        span: Span,\n        input: &CanonicalQueryInput<'tcx, T>,\n    ) -> (InferCtxt<'tcx>, T, CanonicalVarValues<'tcx>)\n    where\n        T: TypeFoldable<TyCtxt<'tcx>>,\n    {\n        let infcx = self.build(input.typing_mode);\n        let (value, args) = infcx.instantiate_canonical(span, &input.canonical);\n        (infcx, value, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn build_with_typing_env(\n        mut self,\n        TypingEnv { typing_mode, param_env }: TypingEnv<'tcx>,\n    ) -> (InferCtxt<'tcx>, ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>) {\n        (self.build(typing_mode), param_env)\n    }\n\n    pub fn build(&mut self, typing_mode: TypingMode<'tcx>) -> InferCtxt<'tcx> {\n        let InferCtxtBuilder {\n            tcx,\n            considering_regions,\n            in_hir_typeck,\n            skip_leak_check,\n            next_trait_solver,\n        } = *self;\n        InferCtxt {\n            tcx,\n            typing_mode,\n            considering_regions,\n            in_hir_typeck,\n            skip_leak_check,\n            inner: RefCell::new(InferCtxtInner::new()),\n            lexical_region_resolutions: RefCell::new(None),\n            selection_cache: Default::default(),\n            evaluation_cache: Default::default(),\n            reported_trait_errors: Default::default(),\n            reported_signature_mismatch: Default::default(),\n            tainted_by_errors: Cell::new(None),\n            universe: Cell::new(ty::UniverseIndex::ROOT),\n            next_trait_solver,\n            obligation_inspector: Cell::new(None),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx, T> InferOk<'tcx, T> {\n    /// Extracts `value`, registering any obligations into `fulfill_cx`.\n    pub fn into_value_registering_obligations<E: 'tcx>(\n        self,\n        infcx: &InferCtxt<'tcx>,\n        fulfill_cx: &mut dyn TraitEngine<'tcx, E>,\n    ) -> T {\n        let InferOk { value, obligations } = self;\n        fulfill_cx.register_predicate_obligations(infcx, obligations);\n        value\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> InferOk<'tcx, ()> {\n    pub fn into_obligations(self) -> PredicateObligations<'tcx> {\n        self.obligations\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> InferCtxt<'tcx> {\n    pub fn dcx(&self) -> DiagCtxtHandle<'_> {\n        self.tcx.dcx().taintable_handle(&self.tainted_by_errors)\n    }\n\n    pub fn next_trait_solver(&self) -> bool {\n        self.next_trait_solver\n    }\n\n    #[inline(always)]\n    pub fn typing_mode(&self) -> TypingMode<'tcx> {\n        self.typing_mode\n    }\n\n    pub fn freshen<T: TypeFoldable<TyCtxt<'tcx>>>(&self, t: T) -> T {\n        t.fold_with(&mut self.freshener())\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the origin of the type variable identified by `vid`.\n    ///\n    /// No attempt is made to resolve `vid` to its root variable.\n    pub fn type_var_origin(&self, vid: TyVid) -> TypeVariableOrigin {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().var_origin(vid)\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the origin of the const variable identified by `vid`\n    // FIXME: We should store origins separately from the unification table\n    // so this doesn't need to be optional.\n    pub fn const_var_origin(&self, vid: ConstVid) -> Option<ConstVariableOrigin> {\n        match self.inner.borrow_mut().const_unification_table().probe_value(vid) {\n            ConstVariableValue::Known { .. } => None,\n            ConstVariableValue::Unknown { origin, .. } => Some(origin),\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn freshener<'b>(&'b self) -> TypeFreshener<'b, 'tcx> {\n        freshen::TypeFreshener::new(self)\n    }\n\n    pub fn unresolved_variables(&self) -> Vec<Ty<'tcx>> {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.borrow_mut();\n        let mut vars: Vec<Ty<'_>> = inner\n            .type_variables()\n            .unresolved_variables()\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|t| Ty::new_var(self.tcx, t))\n            .collect();\n        vars.extend(\n            (0..inner.int_unification_table().len())\n                .map(|i| ty::IntVid::from_usize(i))\n                .filter(|&vid| inner.int_unification_table().probe_value(vid).is_unknown())\n                .map(|v| Ty::new_int_var(self.tcx, v)),\n        );\n        vars.extend(\n            (0..inner.float_unification_table().len())\n                .map(|i| ty::FloatVid::from_usize(i))\n                .filter(|&vid| inner.float_unification_table().probe_value(vid).is_unknown())\n                .map(|v| Ty::new_float_var(self.tcx, v)),\n        );\n        vars\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    pub fn sub_regions(\n        &self,\n        origin: SubregionOrigin<'tcx>,\n        sub_ty: ty::Region<'tcx>,\n        super_ty: ty::Region<'tcx>,\n    ) {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().unwrap_region_constraints().make_subregion(origin, a, b);\n    }\n\n    /// Processes a `Coerce` predicate from the fulfillment context.\n    /// This is NOT the preferred way to handle coercion, which is to\n    /// invoke `FnCtxt::coerce` or a similar method (see `coercion.rs`).\n    ///\n    /// This method here is actually a fallback that winds up being\n    /// invoked when `FnCtxt::coerce` encounters unresolved type variables\n    /// and records a coercion predicate. Presently, this method is equivalent\n    /// to `subtype_predicate` -- that is, \"coercing\" `a` to `b` winds up\n    /// actually requiring `a <: b`. This is of course a valid coercion,\n    /// but it's not as flexible as `FnCtxt::coerce` would be.\n    ///\n    /// (We may refactor this in the future, but there are a number of\n    /// practical obstacles. Among other things, `FnCtxt::coerce` presently\n    /// records adjustments that are required on the HIR in order to perform\n    /// the coercion, and we don't currently have a way to manage that.)\n    pub fn coerce_predicate(\n        &self,\n        cause: &ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n        param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>,\n        predicate: ty::PolyCoercePredicate<'tcx>,\n    ) -> Result<InferResult<'tcx, ()>, (TyVid, TyVid)> {\n        let subtype_predicate = predicate.map_bound(|p| ty::SubtypeRelation {\n            a_is_expected: false, // when coercing from `a` to `b`, `b` is expected\n            sub_ty: p.sub_ty,\n            super_ty: p.super_ty,\n        });\n        self.subtype_predicate(cause, param_env, subtype_predicate)\n    }\n\n    pub fn subtype_predicate(\n        &self,\n        cause: &ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n        param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>,\n        predicate: ty::PolySubtypePredicate<'tcx>,\n    ) -> Result<InferResult<'tcx, ()>, (TyVid, TyVid)> {\n        // Check for two unresolved inference variables, in which case we can\n        // make no progress. This is partly a micro-optimization, but it's\n        // also an opportunity to \"sub-unify\" the variables. This isn't\n        // *necessary* to prevent cycles, because they would eventually be sub-unified\n        // anyhow during generalization, but it helps with diagnostics (we can detect\n        // earlier that they are sub-unified).\n        //\n        // Note that we can just skip the binders here because\n        // type variables can't (at present, at\n        // least) capture any of the things bound by this binder.\n        //\n        // Note that this sub here is not just for diagnostics - it has semantic\n        // effects as well.\n        let r_a = self.shallow_resolve(predicate.skip_binder().sub_ty);\n        let r_b = self.shallow_resolve(predicate.skip_binder().super_ty);\n        match (r_a.kind(), r_b.kind()) {\n            (&ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(a_vid)), &ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(b_vid))) => {\n                self.sub_unify_ty_vids_raw(a_vid, b_vid);\n                return Err((a_vid, b_vid));\n            }\n            _ => {}\n        }\n\n        self.enter_forall(predicate, |ty::SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty }| {\n            if a_is_expected {\n                Ok(self.at(cause, param_env).sub(DefineOpaqueTypes::Yes, a, b))\n            } else {\n                Ok(self.at(cause, param_env).sup(DefineOpaqueTypes::Yes, b, a))\n            }\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Number of type variables created so far.\n    pub fn num_ty_vars(&self) -> usize {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().num_vars()\n    }\n\n    pub fn next_ty_vid(&self, span: Span) -> TyVid {\n        self.next_ty_vid_with_origin(TypeVariableOrigin { span, param_def_id: None })\n    }\n\n    pub fn next_ty_vid_with_origin(&self, origin: TypeVariableOrigin) -> TyVid {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().new_var(self.universe(), origin)\n    }\n\n    pub fn next_ty_vid_in_universe(&self, span: Span, universe: ty::UniverseIndex) -> TyVid {\n        let origin = The generic parameters are\n                // for actual parameters that may be referred to by\n                // the default of this type parameter, if it exists.\n                // e.g., `struct Foo<A, B, C = (A, B)>(...);` when\n                // used in a path such as `Foo::<T, U>::new()` will\n                // use an inference variable for `C` with `[T, U]`\n                // as the generic parameters for the default, `(T, U)`.\n                let ty_var_id = self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().new_var(\n                    self.universe(),\n                    TypeVariableOrigin { param_def_id: Some(param.def_id), span },\n                );\n\n                Ty::new_var(self.tcx, ty_var_id).into()\n            }\n            GenericParamDefKind::Const { .. } => {\n                let origin = ConstVariableOrigin { param_def_id: Some(param.def_id), span };\n                let const_var_id = self\n                    .inner\n                    .borrow_mut()\n                    .const_unification_table()\n                    .new_key(ConstVariableValue::Unknown { origin, universe: self.universe() })\n                    .vid;\n                ty::Const::new_var(self.tcx, const_var_id).into()\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Given a set of generics defined on a type or impl, returns the generic parameters mapping\n    /// each type/region parameter to a fresh inference variable.\n    pub fn fresh_args_for_item(&self, span: Span, def_id: DefId) -> GenericArgsRef<'tcx> {\n        GenericArgs::for_item(self.tcx, def_id, |param, _| self.var_for_def(span, param))\n    }\n\n    /// Returns `true` if errors have been reported since this infcx was\n    /// created.      assert!(storage.data.is_empty(), \"{:#?}\", storage.data);\n        // We clone instead of taking because borrowck still wants to use the\n        // inference context after calling this for diagnostics and the new\n        // trait solver.\n        storage.var_infos.clone()\n    }\n\n    pub fn has_opaque_types_in_storage(&self) -> bool {\n        !self.inner.borrow().opaque_type_storage.is_empty()\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self), ret)]\n    pub fn take_opaque_types(&self) -> Vec<(OpaqueTypeKey<'tcx>, has_opaques_with_sub_unified_hidden_type(&self, ty_vid: TyVid) -> bool {\n        if !self.next_trait_solver() {\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        let ty_sub_vid = self.sub_unification_table_root_var(ty_vid);\n        let inner = &mut *self.inner.borrow_mut();\n        let mut type_variables = inner.type_variable_storage.with_log(&mut inner.undo_log);\n        inner.opaque_type_storage.iter_opaque_types().any(|(_, hidden_ty)| {\n            if let ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(hidden_vid)) = *hidden_ty.ty.kind() {\n                let opaque_sub_vid = type_variables.sub_unification_table_root_var(hidden_vid);\n                if opaque_sub_vid == ty_sub_vid {\n                    return true;\n                }\n            }\n\n            false\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Searches for an opaque type key whose hidden type is related to `ty_vid`.\n    ///\n    /// This only checks for a subtype relation, it does not require equality.\n    pub fn opaques_with_sub_unified_hidden_type(&self, ty_vid: TyVid) -> Vec<ty::AliasTy<'tcx>> {\n        // Avoid accidentally allowing more code to compile with the old solver.\n        if !self.next_trait_solver() {\n            return vec![];\n        }\n\n        let ty_sub_vid = self.sub_unification_table_root_var(ty_vid);\n        let inner = &mut *self.inner.borrow_mut();\n        // This is iffy, can't call `type_variables()` as we're already\n        // borrowing the `opaque_type_storage` here.\n        let mut type_variables = inner.type_variable_storage.with_log(&mut inner.undo_log);\n        inner\n            .opaque_type_storage\n            .iter_opaque_types()\n            .filter_map(|(key, hidden_ty)| {\n                if let ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(hidden_vid)) = *hidden_ty.ty.kind() {\n                    let opaque_sub_vid = type_variables.sub_unification_table_root_var(hidden_vid);\n                    if opaque_sub_vid == ty_sub_vid {\n                        return Some(ty::AliasTy::new_from_args(\n                            self.tcx,\n                            key.def_id.into(),\n                            key.args,\n                        ));\n                    }\n                }\n\n                None\n            })\n            .collect()\n    }\n\n    #[inline(always)]\n    pub fn can_define_opaque_ty(&self, id: impl Into<DefId>) -> bool {\n        debug_assert!(!self.next_trait_solver());\n        match self.typing_mode() {\n            TypingMode::Analysis {\n                defining_opaque_types_and_generators: defining_opaque_types,\n            }\n            | TypingMode::Borrowck { defining_opaque_types } => {\n                id.into().as_local().is_some_and(|def_id| defining_opaque_types.contains(&def_id))\n            }\n            // FIXME(#132279): This function is quite weird in post-analysis\n            // and post-borrowck analysis mode. We may need to modify its uses\n            // to support PostBorrowckAnalysis in the old solver as well.\n            TypingMode::Coherence\n            | TypingMode::PostBorrowckAnalysis { .. }\n            | TypingMode::PostAnalysis => false,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn push_hir_typeck_potentially_region_dependent_goal(\n        &self,\n        goal: PredicateObligation<'tcx>,\n    ) {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.borrow_mut();\n        inner.undo_log.push(UndoLog::PushHirTypeckPotentiallyRegionDependentGoal);\n        inner.hir_typeck_potentially_region_dependent_goals.push(goal);\n    }\n\n    pub fn take_hir_typeck_potentially_region_dependent_goals(\n        &self,\n    ) -> Vec<PredicateObligation<'tcx>> {\n        assert!(!self.in_snapshot(), \"cannot take goals in a snapshot\");\n        std::mem::take(&mut self.inner.borrow_mut().hir_typeck_potentially_region_dependent_goals)\n    }\n\n    pub fn ty_to_string(&self, t: Ty<'tcx>) -> String {\n        self.resolve_vars_if_possible(t).to_string()\n    }\n\n    /// If `TyVar(vid)` resolves to a type, return that type. Else, return the\n    /// universe index of `TyVar(vid)`.\n    pub fn probe_ty_var(&self, vid: TyVid) -> Result<Ty<'tcx>, ty::UniverseIndex> {\n        use self::type_variable::TypeVariableValue;\n\n        match self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().probe(vid) {\n            TypeVariableValue::Known { value } => Ok(value),\n            TypeVariableValue::Unknown { universe } => Err(universe),\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn shallow_resolve(&self, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n        if let ty::Infer(v) = *ty.kind() {\n            match v {\n                ty::TyVar(v) => {\n                    // Not entirely obvious: if `typ` is a type variable,\n                    // it can be resolved to an int/float variable, which\n                    // can then be recursively resolved, hence the\n                    // recursion. Note though that we prevent type\n                    // variables from unifying to other type variables\n                    // directly (though they may be embedded\n                    // structurally), and we prevent cycles in any case,\n                    // so this recursion should always be of very limited\n                    // depth.\n                    //\n                    // Note: if these two lines are combined into one we get\n                    // dynamic borrow errors on `self.inner`.\n                    let known = self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().probe(v).known();\n                    known.map_or(ty, |t| self.shallow_resolve(t))\n                }\n\n                ty::IntVar(v) => {\n                    match self.inner.borrow_mut().int_unification_table().probe_value(v) {\n                        ty::IntVarValue::IntType(ty) => Ty::new_int(self.tcx, ty),\n                        ty::IntVarValue::UintType(ty) => Ty::new_uint(self.tcx, ty),\n                        ty::IntVarValue::Unknown => ty,\n                    }\n                }\n\n                ty::FloatVar(v) => {\n                    match self.inner.borrow_mut().float_unification_table().probe_value(v) {\n                        ty::FloatVarValue::Known(ty) => Ty::new_float(self.tcx, ty),\n                        ty::FloatVarValue::Unknown => ty,\n                    }\n                }\n\n                ty::FreshTy(_) | ty::FreshIntTy(_) | ty::FreshFloatTy(_) => ty,\n            }\n        } else {\n            ty\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn shallow_resolve_const(&self, ct: ty::Const<'tcx>) -> ty::Const<'tcx> {\n        match ct.kind() {\n            ty::ConstKind::Infer(infer_ct) => match infer_ct {\n                InferConst::Var(vid) => self\n                    .inner\n                    .borrow_mut()\n                    .const_unification_table()\n                    .probe_value(vid)\n                    .known()\n                    .unwrap_or(ct),\n                InferConst::Fresh(_) => ct,\n            },\n            ty::ConstKind::Param(_)\n            | ty::ConstKind::Bound(_, _)\n            | ty::ConstKind::Placeholder(_)\n            | ty::ConstKind::Unevaluated(_)\n            | ty::ConstKind::Value(_)\n            | ty::ConstKind::Error(_)\n            | ty::ConstKind::Expr(_) => ct,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn shallow_resolve_term(&self, term: ty::Term<'tcx>) -> ty::Term<'tcx> {\n        match term.kind() {\n            ty::TermKind::Ty(ty) => self.shallow_resolve(ty).into(),\n            ty::TermKind::Const(ct) => self.shallow_resolve_const(ct).into(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn root_var(&self, var: ty::TyVid) -> ty::TyVid {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().root_var(var)\n    }\n\n    pub fn sub_unify_ty_vids_raw(&self, sub_ty: ty::TyVid, super_ty: ty::TyVid) {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().sub_unify(a, b);\n    }\n\n    pub fn sub_unification_table_root_var(&self, var: ty::TyVid) -> ty::TyVid {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().sub_unification_table_root_var(var)\n    }\n\n    pub fn root_const_var(&self, var: ty::ConstVid) -> ty::ConstVid {\n        self.inner.borrow_mut().const_unification_table().find(var).vid\n    }\n\n    /// Resolves an int var to a rigid int type, if it was constrained to one,\n    /// or else the root int var in the unification table.\n    pub fn opportunistic_resolve_int_var(&self, vid: ty::IntVid) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.borrow_mut();\n        let value = inner.int_unification_table().probe_value(vid);\n        match value {\n            ty::IntVarValue::IntType(ty) => Ty::new_int(self.tcx, ty),\n            ty::IntVarValue::UintType(ty) => Ty::new_uint(self.tcx, ty),\n            ty::IntVarValue::Unknown => {\n                Ty::new_int_var(self.tcx, inner.int_unification_table().find(vid))\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Resolves a float var to a rigid int type, if it was constrained to one,\n    /// or else the root float var in the unification table.\n    pub fn opportunistic_resolve_float_var(&self, vid: ty::FloatVid) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.borrow_mut();\n        let value = inner.float_unification_table().probe_value(vid);\n        match value {\n            ty::FloatVarValue::Known(ty) => Ty::new_float(self.tcx, ty),\n            ty::FloatVarValue::Unknown => {\n                Ty::new_float_var(self.tcx, inner.float_unification_table().find(vid))\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Where possible, replaces type/const variables in\n    /// `value` with their final value. Note that region variables\n    /// are unaffected. If a type/const variable has not been unified, it\n    /// is left as is. This is an idempotent operation that does\n    /// not affect inference state in any way and so you can do it\n    /// at will.\n    pub fn resolve_vars_if_possible<T>(&self, value: T) -> T\n    where\n        T: TypeFoldable<TyCtxt<'tcx>>,\n    {\n        if let Err(guar) = value.error_reported() {\n            self.set_tainted_by_errors(guar);\n        }\n        if !value.has_non_region_infer() {\n            return value;\n        }\n        let mut r = resolve::OpportunisticVarResolver::new(self);\n        value.fold_with(&mut r)\n    }\n\n    pub fn resolve_numeric_literals_with_default<T>(&self, value: T) -> T\n    where\n        T: TypeFoldable<TyCtxt<'tcx>>,\n    {\n        if !value.has_infer() {\n            return value; // Avoid duplicated type-folding.\n        }\n        let mut r = InferenceLiteralEraser { tcx: self.tcx };\n        value.fold_with(&mut r)\n    }\n\n    pub fn probe_const_var(&self, vid: ty::ConstVid) -> Result<ty::Const<'tcx>, ty::UniverseIndex> {\n        match self.inner.borrow_mut().const_unification_table().probe_value(vid) {\n            ConstVariableValue::Known { value } => Ok(value),\n            ConstVariableValue::Unknown { origin: _, universe } => Err(universe),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Attempts to resolve all type/region/const variables in\n    /// `value`. Region inference must have been run already (e.g.,\n    /// by calling `resolve_regions_and_report_errors`). If some\n    /// variable was never unified, an `Err` results.\n    ///\n    /// This method is idempotent, but it not typically not invoked\n    /// except during the writeback phase.\n    pub fn fully_resolve<T: TypeFoldable<TyCtxt<'tcx>>>(&self, value: T) -> FixupResult<T> {\n        match resolve::fully_resolve(self, value) {\n            Ok(value) => {\n                if value.has_non_region_infer() {\n                    bug!(\"`{value:?}` is not fully resolved\");\n                }\n                if value.has_infer_regions() {\n                    let guar = self.dcx().delayed_bug(format!(\"`{value:?}` is not fully resolved\"));\n                    Ok(fold_regions(self.tcx, value, |re, _| {\n                        if re.is_var() { ty::Region::new_error(self.tcx, guar) } else { re }\n                    }))\n                } else {\n                    Ok(value)\n                }\n            }\n            Err(e) => Err(e),\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Instantiates the bound variables in a given binder with fresh inference\n    // variables in the current universe.\n    //\n    // Use this method if you'd like to find some generic parameters of the binder's\n    // variables (e.g. during a method call). If there isn't a [`BoundRegionConversionTime`]\n    // that corresponds to your use case, consider whether or not you should\n    // use [`InferCtxt::enter_forall`] instead.\n    pub fn instantiate_binder_with_fresh_vars<T>(\n        &self,\n        span: Span,\n        lbrct: BoundRegionConversionTime,\n        value: ty::Binder<'tcx, T>,\n    ) -> T\n    where\n        T: TypeFoldable<TyCtxt<'tcx>> + Copy,\n    {\n        if let Some(inner) = value.no_bound_vars() {\n            return inner;\n        }\n\n        let bound_vars = value.bound_vars();\n        let mut args = Vec::with_capacity(bound_vars.len());\n\n        for bound_var_kind in bound_vars {\n            let arg: ty::GenericArg<'_> = match bound_var_kind {\n                ty::BoundVariableKind::Ty(_) => self.next_ty_var(span).into(),\n                ty::BoundVariableKind::Region(br) => {\n                    self.next_region_var(RegionVariableOrigin::BoundRegion(span, br, lbrct)).into()\n                }\n                ty::BoundVariableKind::Const => self.next_const_var(span).into(),\n            };\n            args.push(arg);\n        }\n\n        struct ToFreshVars<'tcx> {\n            args: Vec<ty::GenericArg<'tcx>>,\n        }\n\n        impl<'tcx> BoundVarReplacerDelegate<'tcx> for ToFreshVars<'tcx> {\n            fn replace_region(&mut self, br: ty::BoundRegion) -> ty::Region<'tcx> {\n                self.args[br.var.index()].expect_region()\n            }\n            fn replace_ty(&mut self, bt: ty::BoundTy) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n                self.args[bt.var.index()].expect_ty()\n            }\n            fn replace_const(&mut self, bc: ty::BoundConst) -> ty::Const<'tcx> {\n                self.args[bc.var.index()].expect_const()\n            }\n        }\n        let delegate = ToFreshVars { args };\n        self.tcx.replace_bound_vars_uncached(value, delegate)\n    }\n\n    /// See the [`region_constraints::RegionConstraintCollector::verify_generic_bound`] method.\n    pub(crate) fn verify_generic_bound(\n        &self,\n        origin: SubregionOrigin<'tcx>,\n        kind: GenericKind<'tcx>,\n        sub_ty: ty::Region<'tcx>,\n        bound: VerifyBound<'tcx>,\n    ) {\n        debug!(\"verify_generic_bound({:?}, {:?} <: {:?})\", kind, a, bound);\n\n        self.inner\n            .borrow_mut()\n            .unwrap_region_constraints()\n            .verify_generic_bound(origin, kind, a, bound);\n    }\n\n    /// Obtains the latest type of the given closure; this may be a\n    /// closure in the current function, in which case its\n    /// `ClosureKind` may not yet be known.\n    pub fn closure_kind(&self, closure_ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Option<ty::ClosureKind> {\n        let unresolved_kind_ty = match *closure_ty.kind() {\n            ty::Closure(_, args) => args.as_closure().kind_ty(),\n            ty::CoroutineClosure(_, args) => args.as_coroutine_closure().kind_ty(),\n            _ => bug!(\"unexpected type {closure_ty}\"),\n        };\n        let closure_kind_ty = self.shallow_resolve(unresolved_kind_ty);\n        closure_kind_ty.to_opt_closure_kind()\n    }\n\n    pub fn universe(&self) -> ty::UniverseIndex {\n        self.universe.get()\n    }\n\n    /// Creates and return a fresh universe that extends all previous\n    /// universes. Updates `self.universe` to that new universe.\n    pub fn create_next_universe(&self) -> ty::UniverseIndex {\n        let u = self.universe.get().next_universe();\n        debug!(\"create_next_universe {u:?}\");\n        self.universe.set(u);\n        u\n    }\n\n    /// Extract [`ty::TypingMode`] of this inference context to get a `TypingEnv`\n    /// which contains the necessary information to use the trait system without\n    /// using canonicalization or carrying this inference context around.\n    pub fn typing_env(&self, param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>) -> ty::TypingEnv<'tcx> {\n        let typing_mode = match self.typing_mode() {\n            // FIXME(#132279): This erases the `defining_opaque_types` as it isn't possible\n            // to handle them without proper canonicalization. This means we may cause cycle\n            // errors and fail to reveal opaques while inside of bodies. We should rename this\n            // function and require explicit comments on all use-sites in the future.\n            ty::TypingMode::Analysis { defining_opaque_types_and_generators: _ }\n            | ty::TypingMode::Borrowck { defining_opaque_types: _ } => {\n                TypingMode::non_body_analysis()\n            }\n            mode @ (ty::TypingMode::Coherence\n            | ty::TypingMode::PostBorrowckAnalysis { .. }\n            | ty::TypingMode::PostAnalysis) => mode,\n        };\n        ty::TypingEnv { typing_mode, param_env }\n    }\n\n    /// Similar to [`Self::canonicalize_query`], except that it returns\n    /// a [`PseudoCanonicalInput`] and requires both the `value` and the\n    /// `param_env` to not contain any inference variables or placeholders.\n    pub fn pseudo_canonicalize_query<V>(\n        &self,\n        param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>,\n        value: V,\n    ) -> PseudoCanonicalInput<'tcx, V>\n    where\n        V: TypeVisitable<TyCtxt<'tcx>>,\n    {\n        debug_assert!(!value.has_infer());\n        debug_assert!(!value.has_placeholders());\n        debug_assert!(!param_env.has_infer());\n        debug_assert!(!param_env.has_placeholders());\n        self.typing_env(param_env).as_query_input(value)\n    }\n\n    /// The returned function is used in a fast path. If it returns `true` the variable is\n    /// unchanged, `false` indicates that the status is unknown.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn is_ty_infer_var_definitely_unchanged(&self) -> impl Fn(TyOrConstInferVar) -> bool {\n        // This hoists the borrow/release out of the loop body.\n        let inner = self.inner.try_borrow();\n\n        move |infer_var: TyOrConstInferVar| match (infer_var, &inner) {\n            (TyOrConstInferVar::Ty(ty_var), Ok(inner)) => {\n                use self::type_variable::TypeVariableValue;\n\n                matches!(\n                    inner.try_type_variables_probe_ref(ty_var),\n                    Some(TypeVariableValue::Unknown { .. })\n                )\n            }\n            _ => false,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// `ty_or_const_infer_var_changed` is equivalent to one of these two:\n    ///   * `shallow_resolve(ty) != ty` (where `ty.kind = ty::Infer(_)`)\n    ///   * `shallow_resolve(ct) != ct` (where `ct.kind = ty::ConstKind::Infer(_)`)\n    ///\n    /// However, `ty_or_const_infer_var_changed` is more efficient. It's always\n    /// inlined, despite being large, because it has only two call sites that\n    /// are extremely hot (both in `traits::fulfill`'s checking of `stalled_on`\n    /// inference variables), and it handles both `Ty` and `ty::Const` without\n    /// having to resort to storing full `GenericArg`s in `stalled_on`.\n    #[inline(always)]\n    pub fn ty_or_const_infer_var_changed(&self, infer_var: TyOrConstInferVar) -> bool {\n        match infer_var {\n            TyOrConstInferVar::Ty(v) => {\n                use self::type_variable::TypeVariableValue;\n\n                // If `inlined_probe` returns a `Known` value, it never equals\n                // `ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(v))`.\n                match self.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().inlined_probe(v) {\n                    TypeVariableValue::Unknown { .. } => false,\n                    TypeVariableValue::Known { .. } => true,\n                }\n            }\n\n            TyOrConstInferVar::TyInt(v) => {\n                // If `inlined_probe_value` returns a value it's always a\n                // `ty::Int(_)` or `ty::UInt(_)`, which never matches a\n                // `ty::Infer(_)`.\n                self.inner.borrow_mut().int_unification_table().inlined_probe_value(v).is_known()\n            }\n\n            TyOrConstInferVar::TyFloat(v) => {\n                // If `probe_value` returns a value it's always a\n                // `ty::Float(_)`, which never matches a `ty::Infer(_)`.\n                //\n                // Not `inlined_probe_value(v)` because this call site is colder.\n                self.inner.borrow_mut().float_unification_table().probe_value(v).is_known()\n            }\n\n            TyOrConstInferVar::Const(v) => {\n                // If `probe_value` returns a `Known` value, it never equals\n                // `ty::ConstKind::Infer(ty::InferConst::Var(v))`.\n                //\n                // Not `inlined_probe_value(v)` because this call site is colder.\n                match self.inner.borrow_mut().const_unification_table().probe_value(v) {\n                    ConstVariableValue::Unknown { .. } => false,\n                    ConstVariableValue::Known { .. } => true,\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Attach a callback to be invoked on each root obligation evaluated in the new trait solver.\n    pub fn attach_obligation_inspector(&self, inspector: ObligationInspector<'tcx>) {\n        debug_assert!(\n            self.obligation_inspector.get().is_none(),\n            \"shouldn't override a set obligation inspector\"\n        );\n        self.obligation_inspector.set(Some(inspector));\n    }\n}\n\n/// Helper for [InferCtxt::ty_or_const_infer_var_changed] (see comment on that), currently\n/// used only for `traits::fulfill`'s list of `stalled_on` inference variables.\n#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\npub enum TyOrConstInferVar {\n    /// Equivalent to `ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(_))`.\n    Ty(TyVid),\n    /// Equivalent to `ty::Infer(ty::IntVar(_))`.\n    TyInt(IntVid),\n    /// Equivalent to `ty::Infer(ty::FloatVar(_))`.\n    TyFloat(FloatVid),\n\n    /// Equivalent to `ty::ConstKind::Infer(ty::InferConst::Var(_))`.\n    Const(ConstVid),\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> TyOrConstInferVar {\n    /// Tries to extract an inference variable from a type or a constant, returns `None`\n    /// for types other than `ty::Infer(_)` (or `InferTy::Fresh*`) and\n    /// for constants other than `ty::ConstKind::Infer(_)` (or `InferConst::Fresh`).\n    pub fn maybe_from_generic_arg(arg: GenericArg<'tcx>) -> Option<Self> {\n        match arg.kind() {\n            GenericArgKind::Type(ty) => Self::maybe_from_ty(ty),\n            GenericArgKind::Const(ct) => Self::maybe_from_const(ct),\n            GenericArgKind::Lifetime(_) => None,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Tries to extract an inference variable from a type or a constant, returns `None`\n    /// for types other than `ty::Infer(_)` (or `InferTy::Fresh*`) and\n    /// for constants other than `ty::ConstKind::Infer(_)` (or `InferConst::Fresh`).\n    pub fn maybe_from_term(term: Term<'tcx>) -> Option<Self> {\n        match term.kind() {\n            TermKind::Ty(ty) => Self::maybe_from_ty(ty),\n            TermKind::Const(ct) => Self::maybe_from_const(ct),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Tries to extract an inference variable from a type, returns `None`\n    /// for types other than `ty::Infer(_)` (or `InferTy::Fresh*`).\n    fn maybe_from_ty(ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Option<Self> {\n        match *ty.kind() {\n            ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(v)) => Some(TyOrConstInferVar::Ty(v)),\n            ty::Infer(ty::IntVar(v)) => Some(TyOrConstInferVar::TyInt(v)),\n            ty::Infer(ty::FloatVar(v)) => Some(TyOrConstInferVar::TyFloat(v)),\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Tries to extract an inference variable from a constant, returns `None`\n    /// for constants other than `ty::ConstKind::Infer(_)` (or `InferConst::Fresh`).\n    fn maybe_from_const(ct: ty::Const<'tcx>) -> Option<Self> {\n        match ct.kind() {\n            ty::ConstKind::Infer(InferConst::Var(v)) => Some(TyOrConstInferVar::Const(v)),\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Replace `{integer}` with `i32` and `{float}` with `f64`.\n/// Used only for diagnostics.\nstruct InferenceLiteralEraser<'tcx> {\n    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> TypeFolder<TyCtxt<'tcx>> for InferenceLiteralEraser<'tcx> {\n    fn cx(&self) -> TyCtxt<'tcx> {\n        self.tcx\n    }\n\n    fn fold_ty(&mut self, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n        match ty.kind() {\n            ty::Infer(ty::IntVar(_) | ty::FreshIntTy(_)) => self.tcx.types.i32,\n            ty::Infer(ty::FloatVar(_) | ty::FreshFloatTy(_)) => self.tcx.types.f64,\n            _ => ty.super_fold_with(self),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> TypeTrace<'tcx> {\n    pub fn span(&self) -> Span {\n        self.cause.span\n    }\n\n    pub fn types(cause: &ObligationCause<'tcx>, sub_ty: Ty<'tcx>, super_ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> TypeTrace<'tcx> {\n        TypeTrace {\n            cause: cause.clone(),\n            values: ValuePairs::Terms(ExpectedFound::new(a.into(), b.into())),\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_refs(\n        cause: &ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n        sub_ty: ty::TraitRef<'tcx>,\n        super_ty: ty::TraitRef<'tcx>,\n    ) -> TypeTrace<'tcx> {\n        TypeTrace { cause: cause.clone(), values: ValuePairs::TraitRefs(ExpectedFound::new(sub_ty, super_ty)) }\n    }\n\n    pub fn consts(\n        cause: &ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n        sub_ty: ty::Const<'tcx>,\n        super_ty: ty::Const<'tcx>,\n    ) -> TypeTrace<'tcx> {\n        TypeTrace {\n            cause: cause.clone(),\n            values: ValuePairs::Terms(ExpectedFound::new(a.into(), b.into())),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> SubregionOrigin<'tcx> {\n    pub fn span(&self) -> Span {\n        match *self {\n            SubregionOrigin::Subtype(ref a) => a.span(),\n            SubregionOrigin::RelateObjectBound(a) => a,\n            SubregionOrigin::RelateParamBound(a, ..) => a,\n            SubregionOrigin::RelateRegionParamBound(a, _) => a,\n            SubregionOrigin::Reborrow(a) => a,\n            SubregionOrigin::ReferenceOutlivesReferent(_, a) => a,\n            SubregionOrigin::CompareImplItemObligation { span, .. } => span,\n            SubregionOrigin::AscribeUserTypeProvePredicate(span) => span,\n            SubregionOrigin::CheckAssociatedTypeBounds { ref parent, .. } => parent.span(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn infcx: &'infcx InferCtxt<'tcx>,\n\n    // Immutable fields\n    trace: TypeTrace<'tcx>,\n    param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>,\n    define_opaque_types: DefineOpaqueTypes,\n\n    // Mutable fields.\n meaningfully changes\n    /// the result when relating types.\n    ///\n    /// The cache does not track whether the state of the\n    /// `InferCtxt` has been changed or whether we've added any\n    /// obligations to `self.goals`. Whether a goal is added\n    /// once or multiple times is not really meaningful.\n    ///\n    /// Changes in the inference state may delay some type inference to\n    /// the next fulfillment loop. Given that this loop is already\n    /// necessary, this is also not a meaningful change. Consider\n    /// the following three relations:\n    /// ```text\n    /// Vec<?0> sub Vec<?1>\n    /// ?0 eq u32\n    /// Vec<?0> sub Vec<?1>\n    /// ```\n    /// Without a cache, the second `Vec<?0> sub Vec<?1>` would eagerly\n    /// constrain `?1` to `u32`. When using the cache entry from the\n    /// first time we've related these types, this only happens when\n    /// later proving the `Subtype(?0, ?1)` goal from the first relation.\n    cache:        ty::Binder::dummy(ty::PredicateKind::Subtype(ty::SubtypeRelation {\n                                a_is_expected: true,\n                                a,\n                                b,\n                            })),\n                        ));\n                    }\n                    ty::Contravariant => {\n                        // can't make progress on `B <: A` if both A and B are\n                        // type variables, so record an obligation.\n                        self.obligations.push(Obligation::new(\n                            self.cx(),\n                            self.trace.cause.clone(),\n                            self.param_env,\n                            ty::Binder::dummy(ty::PredicateKind::Subtype(ty::SubtypeRelation {\n                                a_is_expected: false,\n                                sub_ty: b,\n                                super_ty: a,\n                            })),\n                        ));\n                    }\n                    ty::Invariant => {\n                        infcx.inner.borrow_mut().type_variables().equate(a_id, b_id);\n                    }\n                    ty::Bivariant => {\n                        unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n\n            (&ty::Infer(TyVar(a_vid)), _) => {\n                infcx.instantiate_ty_var(self, true, a_vid, self.ambient_variance, b)?;\n            }\n            (_, &ty::Infer(TyVar(b_vid))) => {\n                infcx.instantiate_ty_var(\n                    self,\n                    false,\n                    b_vid,\n                    self.ambient_variance.xform(ty::Contravariant),\n                    a,\n                )?;\n            }\n\n            (\n                &ty::Alias(ty::Opaque, ty::AliasTy { def_id: a_def_id, .. }),\n                &ty::Alias(ty::Opaque, ty::AliasTy { def_id: b_def_id, .. }),\n            ) if a_def_id == b_def_id => {\n                super_combine_tys(infcx, self, a, b)?;\n            }\n\n            (&ty::Alias(ty::Opaque, ty::AliasTy { def_id, .. }), _)\n            | (_, &ty::Alias(ty::Opaque, ty::AliasTy { def_id, .. }))\n                if self.define_opaque_types == DefineOpaqueTypes::Yes && def_id.is_local() =>\n            {\n                self.register_goals(infcx.handle_opaque_type(\n                    a,\n                    b,\n                    self.trace.cause.span,\n                    self.param_env(),\n                )?);\n            }\n\n            _ => {\n                super_combine_tys(infcx, self, a, b)?;\n            }\n        }\n\n        assert!(self.cache.insert((self.ambient_variance, a, b)));\n\n        Ok(a)\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n    fn regions(\n        &mut self,\n        sub_ty: ty::Region<'tcx>,\n        super_ty: ty::Region<'tcx>,\n    ) -> RelateResult<'tcx, ty::Region<'tcx>> {\n        let origin = SubregionOrigin::Subtype(Box::new(self.trace.clone()));\n\n        match self.ambient_variance {\n            // Subtype(&'a u8, &'b u8) => Outlives('sub_ty: 'b) => SubRegion('b, 'a)\n            ty::Covariant => {\n                self.infcx\n                    .inner\n                    .borrow_mut()\n                    .unwrap_region_constraints()\n                    .make_subregion(origin, b, a);\n            }\n            // Suptype(&'a u8, &'b u8) => Outlives('super_ty: 'a) => SubRegion('a, 'b)\n            ty::Contravariant => {\n                self.infcx\n                    .inner\n                    .borrow_mut()\n                    .unwrap_region_constraints()\n                    .make_subregion(origin, a, b);\n            }\n            ty::Invariant => {\n                self.infcx\n                    .inner\n                    .borrow_mut()\n                    .unwrap_region_constraints()\n                    .make_eqregion(origin, a, b);\n            }\n            ty::Bivariant => {\n                unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n            }\n        }\n\n        Ok(a)\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n    fn consts(\n        &mut self,\n        sub_ty: ty::Const<'tcx>,\n        super_ty: ty::Const<'tcx>,\n    ) -> RelateResult<'tcx, ty::Const<'tcx>> {\n        super_combine_consts(self.infcx, self, a, b)\n    }\n\n    fn binders<T>(\n        &mut self,\n        sub_ty: ty::Binder<'tcx, T>,\n        super_ty: ty::Binder<'tcx, T>,\n    ) -> RelateResult<'tcx, ty::Binder<'tcx, T>>\n    where\n        T: Relate<TyCtxt<'tcx>>,\n    {\n        if a == b {\n            // Do nothing\n        } else if let Some(a) = a.no_bound_vars()\n            && let Some(b) = b.no_bound_vars()\n        {\n            self.relate(a, b)?;\n        } else {\n            let span = self.trace.cause.span;\n            let infcx = self.infcx;\n\n            match self.ambient_variance {\n                // Checks whether `for<..> sub <: for<..> sup` holds.\n                //\n                // For this to hold, **all** instantiations of the super type\n                // have to be a super type of **at least one** instantiation of\n                // the subtype.\n                //\n                // This is implemented by first entering a new universe.\n                // We then replace all bound variables in `sup` with placeholders,\n                // and all bound variables in `sub` with inference vars.\n                // We can then just relate the two resulting types as normal.\n                //\n                // Note: this is a subtle algorithm. For a full explanation, please see\n                // the [rustc dev guide][rd]\n                //\n                // [rd]: https://rustc-dev-guide.rust-lang.org/borrow_check/region_inference/placeholders_and_universes.html\n                ty::Covariant => {\n                    infcx.enter_forall(b, |b| {\n                        let a = infcx.instantiate_binder_with_fresh_vars(span, HigherRankedType, a);\n                        self.relate(a, b)\n                    })?;\n                }\n                ty::Contravariant => {\n                    infcx.enter_forall(a, |a| {\n                        let b = infcx.instantiate_binder_with_fresh_vars(span, HigherRankedType, b);\n                        self.relate(a, b)\n                    })?;\n                }\n\n                // When **equating** binders, we check that there is a 1-to-1\n                // correspondence between the bound vars in both types.\n                //\n                // We do so by separately instantiating one of the binders with\n                // placeholders and the other with inference variables and then\n                // equating the instantiated types.\n                //\n                // We want `for<..> A == for<..> B` -- therefore we want\n                // `exists<..> A == for<..> B` and `exists<..> B == for<..> A`.\n                // Check if `exists<..> A == for<..> B`\n                ty::Invariant => {\n                    infcx.enter_forall(b, |b| {\n                        let a = infcx.instantiate_binder_with_fresh_vars(span, HigherRankedType, a);\n                        self.relate(a, b)\n                    })?;\n\n                    // Check if `exists<..> B == for<..> A`.\n                    infcx.enter_forall(a, |a| {\n                        let b = infcx.instantiate_binder_with_fresh_vars(span, HigherRankedType, b);\n                        self.relate(a, b)\n                    })?;\n                }\n                ty::Bivariant => {\n                    unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        Ok(a)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> PredicateEmittingRelation<InferCtxt<'tcx>> for TypeRelating<'_, 'tcx> {\n    fn span(&self) -> Span {\n        self.trace.span()\n    }\n\n    fn param_env(&self) -> ty::ParamEnv<'tcx> {\n        self.param_env\n    }\n\n    fn structurally_relate_aliases(&self) -> StructurallyRelateAliases {\n        StructurallyRelateAliases::No\n    }\n\n    fn register_predicates(\n        &mut self,\n        preds: impl IntoIterator<Item: ty::Upcast<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty::Predicate<'tcx>>>,\n    ) {\n        self.obligations.extend(preds.into_iter().map(|pred| {\n            Obligation::new(self.infcx.tcx, self.trace.cause.clone(), self.param_env, pred)\n        }))\n    }\n\n    fn register_goals(&mut self, goals: impl IntoIterator<Item = Goal<'tcx, ty::Predicate<'tcx>>>) {\n        self.obligations.extend(goals.into_iter().map(|goal| {\n            Obligation::new(\n                self.infcx.tcx,\n                self.trace.cause.clone(),\n                goal.param_env,\n                goal.predicate,\n            )\n        }))\n    }\n\n    fn register_alias_relate_predicate(&mut self, sub_ty: Ty<'tcx>, super_ty: Ty<'tcx>) {\n        self.register_predicates([ty::Binder::dummy(match self.ambient_variance {\n            ty::Covariant => ty::PredicateKind::AliasRelate(\n                a.into(),\n                b.into(),\n                ty::AliasRelationDirection::Subtype,\n            ),\n            // a :> b is b <: a\n            ty::Contravariant => ty::PredicateKind::AliasRelate(\n                b.into(),\n                a.into(),\n                ty::AliasRelationDirection::Subtype,\n            ),\n            ty::Invariant => ty::PredicateKind::AliasRelate(\n                a.into(),\n                b.into(),\n                ty::AliasRelationDirection::Equate,\n            ),\n            ty::Bivariant => {\n                unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n            }\n        })]);\n    }\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":140,"oldLines":8,"newStart":140,"newLines":8,"lines":["                             self.param_env,"," StructurallyRelateAliases,\n    param_env: I::ParamEnv,\n    span: I::Span,\n    // Mutable fields.\n    ambient_variance: ty::Variance,\n    goals: Vec<Goal<I, I::Predicate>>,\n    /// The cache only Whether a goal is added once or multiple\n    /// times is not really meaningful.\n    ///\n    /// Changes in the inference state may delay some type inference to\n    /// the next fulfillment loop. Given that this loop is already\n    /// necessary, this is also not a meaningful change. Consider\n    /// the following three relations:\n    /// ```text\n    /// Vec<?0> sub Vec<?1>\n    /// ?0 eq u32\n    /// Vec<?0> sub Vec<?1>\n    /// ```\n    /// Without a cache, the second `Vec<?0> sub Vec<?1>` would eagerly\n    /// constrain `?1` to `u32`. When using the cache entry from the\n    /// first time we've related these types, this only happens when\n    /// later proving the `Subtype(?0, ?1)` goal from the first relation.\n    cache: DelayedSet<(ty::Variance, I::Ty, I::Ty)>,\n}\n\nimpl<'infcx, Infcx, I> SolverRelating<'infcx, Infcx, I>\nwhere\n    Infcx: InferCtxtLike<Interner = I>,\n    I: Interner,\n{\n    pub fn new(\n        infcx: &'infcx Infcx,\n        structurally_relate_aliases: StructurallyRelateAliases,\n        ambient_variance: ty::Variance,\n        param_env: I::ParamEnv,\n        span: I::Span,\n    ) -> Self {\n        SolverRelating {\n            infcx,\n            structurally_relate_aliases,\n            span,\n            ambient_variance,\n            param_env,\n            goals: vec![],\n            cache: Default::default(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<Infcx, I> TypeRelation<I> for SolverRelating<'_, Infcx, I>\nwhere\n    Infcx: InferCtxtLike<Interner = I>,\n    I: Interner,\n{\n    fn cx(&self) -> I {\n        self.infcx.cx()\n    }\n\n    fn relate_item_args(\n        &mut self,\n        item_def_id: I::DefId,\n        a_arg: I::GenericArgs,\n        b_arg: I::GenericArgs,\n    ) -> RelateResult<I, I::GenericArgs> {\n        if self.ambient_variance == ty::Invariant {\n            // Avoid fetching the variance if we are in an invariant\n            // context; no need, and it can induce dependency cycles\n            // (e.g., #41849).\n            relate_args_invariantly(self, a_arg, b_arg)\n        } else {\n            let tcx = self.cx();\n            let opt_variances = tcx.variances_of(item_def_id);\n            relate_args_with_variances(self, item_def_id, opt_variances, a_arg, b_arg, false)\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn relate_with_variance<T: Relate<I>>(\n        &mut self,\n        variance: ty::Variance,\n        _info: VarianceDiagInfo<I>,\n        sub_ty: T,\n        super_ty: T,\n    ) -> RelateResult<I, T> {\n        let old_ambient_variance = self.ambient_variance;\n        self.ambient_variance = self.ambient_variance.xform(variance);\n        debug!(?self.ambient_variance, \"new ambient variance\");\n\n        let r = if self.ambient_variance == ty::Bivariant { Ok(sub_ty) } else { self.relate(sub_ty, super_ty) };\n\n        self.ambient_variance = old_ambient_variance;\n        r\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n    fn tys(&mut self, sub_ty: I::Ty, super_ty: I::Ty) -> RelateResult<I, I::Ty> {\n        if a == b {\n            return Ok(a);\n        }\n\n        let infcx = self.infcx;\n        let a = infcx.shallow_resolve(a);\n        let b = infcx.shallow_resolve(b);\n\n        if self.cache.contains(&(self.ambient_variance, a, b)) {\n            return Ok(a);\n        }\n\n        match (a.kind(), b.kind()) {\n            (ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(a_id)), ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(b_id))) => {\n                match self.ambient_variance {\n                    ty::Covariant => {\n                        // can't make progress on `A <: B` if both A and B are\n                        // type variables, so record an obligation.\n                        self.goals.push(Goal::new(\n                            self.cx(),\n                            self.param_env,\n                            ty::Binder::dummy(ty::PredicateKind::Subtype(ty::SubtypeRelation {\n                                a_is_expected: true,\n                                a,\n                                b,\n                            })),\n                        ));\n                    }\n                    ty::Contravariant => {\n                        // can't make progress on `B <: A` if both A and B are\n                        // type variables, so record an obligation.\n                        self.goals.push(Goal::new(\n                            self.cx(),\n                            self.param_env,\n                            ty::Binder::dummy(ty::PredicateKind::Subtype(ty::SubtypeRelation {\n                                a_is_expected: false,\n                                sub_ty: b,\n                                super_ty: a,\n                            })),\n                        ));\n                    }\n                    ty::Invariant => {\n                        infcx.equate_ty_vids_raw(a_id, b_id);\n                    }\n                    ty::Bivariant => {\n                        unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n\n            (ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(a_vid)), _) => {\n                infcx.instantiate_ty_var_raw(self, true, a_vid, self.ambient_variance, b)?;\n            }\n            (_, ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(b_vid))) => {\n                infcx.instantiate_ty_var_raw(\n                    self,\n                    false,\n                    b_vid,\n                    self.ambient_variance.xform(ty::Contravariant),\n                    a,\n                )?;\n            }\n\n            _ => {\n                super_combine_tys(self.infcx, self, a, b)?;\n            }\n        }\n\n        assert!(self.cache.insert((self.ambient_variance, a, b)));\n\n        Ok(a)\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n    fn regions(&mut self, sub_ty: I::Region, super_ty: I::Region) -> RelateResult<I, I::Region> {\n        match self.ambient_variance {\n            // Subtype(&'a u8, &'b u8) => Outlives('sub_ty: 'b) => SubRegion('b, 'a)\n            ty::Covariant => self.infcx.sub_regions(b, a, self.span),\n            // Suptype(&'a u8, &'b u8) => Outlives('super_ty: 'a) => SubRegion('a, 'b)\n            ty::Contravariant => self.infcx.sub_regions(a, b, self.span),\n            ty::Invariant => self.infcx.equate_regions(a, b, self.span),\n            ty::Bivariant => {\n                unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n            }\n        }\n\n        Ok(a)\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n    fn consts(&mut self, sub_ty: I::Const, super_ty: I::Const) -> RelateResult<I, I::Const> {\n        super_combine_consts(self.infcx, self, a, b)\n    }\n\n    fn binders<T>(\n        &mut self,\n        sub_ty: ty::Binder<I, T>,\n        super_ty: ty::Binder<I, T>,\n    ) -> RelateResult<I, ty::Binder<I, T>>\n    where\n        T: Relate<I>,\n    {\n        // If they're equal, then short-circuit.\n        if a == b {\n            return Ok(a);\n        }\n\n        // If they have no bound vars, relate normally.\n        if let Some(a_inner) = a.no_bound_vars()\n            && let Some(b_inner) = b.no_bound_vars()\n        {\n            self.relate(a_inner, b_inner)?;\n            return Ok(a);\n        }\n\n        match self.ambient_variance {\n            // Checks whether `for<..> sub <: for<..> sup` holds.\n            //\n            // For this to hold, **all** instantiations of the super type\n            // have to be a super type of **at least one** instantiation of\n            // the subtype.\n            //\n            // This is implemented by first entering a new universe.\n            // We then replace all bound variables in `sup` with placeholders,\n            // and all bound variables in `sub` with inference vars.\n            // We can then just relate the two resulting types as normal.\n            //\n            // Note: this is a subtle algorithm. For a full explanation, please see\n            // the [rustc dev guide][rd]\n            //\n            // [rd]: https://rustc-dev-guide.rust-lang.org/borrow_check/region_inference/placeholders_and_universes.html\n            ty::Covariant => {\n                self.infcx.enter_forall(b, |b| {\n                    let a = self.infcx.instantiate_binder_with_infer(a);\n                    self.relate(a, b)\n                })?;\n            }\n            ty::Contravariant => {\n                self.infcx.enter_forall(a, |a| {\n                    let b = self.infcx.instantiate_binder_with_infer(b);\n                    self.relate(a, b)\n                })?;\n            }\n\n            // When **equating** binders, we check that there is a 1-to-1\n            // correspondence between the bound vars in both types.\n            //\n            // We do so by separately instantiating one of the binders with\n            // placeholders and the other with inference variables and then\n            // equating the instantiated types.\n            //\n            // We want `for<..> A == for<..> B` -- therefore we want\n            // `exists<..> A == for<..> B` and `exists<..> B == for<..> A`.\n            // Check if `exists<..> A == for<..> B`\n            ty::Invariant => {\n                self.infcx.enter_forall(b, |b| {\n                    let a = self.infcx.instantiate_binder_with_infer(a);\n                    self.relate(a, b)\n                })?;\n\n                // Check if `exists<..> B == for<..> A`.\n                self.infcx.enter_forall(a, |a| {\n                    let b = self.infcx.instantiate_binder_with_infer(b);\n                    self.relate(a, b)\n                })?;\n            }\n            ty::Bivariant => {\n                unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n            }\n        }\n        Ok(a)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<Infcx, I> PredicateEmittingRelation<Infcx> for SolverRelating<'_, Infcx, I>\nwhere\n    Infcx: InferCtxtLike<Interner = I>,\n    I: Interner,\n{\n    fn span(&self) -> I::Span {\n        Span::dummy()\n    }\n\n    fn param_env(&self) -> I::ParamEnv {\n        self.param_env\n    }\n\n    fn structurally_relate_aliases(&self) -> StructurallyRelateAliases {\n        self.structurally_relate_aliases\n    }\n\n    fn register_predicates(\n        &mut self,\n        obligations: impl IntoIterator<Item: ty::Upcast<I, I::Predicate>>,\n    ) {\n        self.goals.extend(\n            obligations.into_iter().map(|pred| Goal::new(self.infcx.cx(), self.param_env, pred)),\n        );\n    }\n\n    fn register_goals(&mut self, obligations: impl IntoIterator<Item = Goal<I, I::Predicate>>) {\n        self.goals.extend(obligations);\n    }\n\n    fn register_alias_relate_predicate(&mut self, sub_ty: I::Ty, super_ty: I::Ty) {\n        self.register_predicates([ty::Binder::dummy(match self.ambient_variance {\n            ty::Covariant => ty::PredicateKind::AliasRelate(\n                a.into(),\n                b.into(),\n                ty::AliasRelationDirection::Subtype,\n            ),\n            // a :> b is b <: a\n            ty::Contravariant => ty::PredicateKind::AliasRelate(\n                b.into(),\n              ty::AliasRelationDirection::Equate,\n            ),\n            ty::Bivariant => {\n                unreachable!(\"Expected bivariance to be handled in relate_with_variance\")\n       V: rustc_type_ir::TypeFoldable<Self::Interner>,\n    {\n        canonical.instantiate(self.cx(), &values)\n    }\n\n    fn instantiate_canonical_var(\n        &self,\n        kind:       def_id: SolverDefId,\n        args: GenericArgs<'db>,\n        param_env: ParamEnv<'db>,\n        hidden_ty: Ty<'db>,\n        goals: &mut Vec<Goal<'db, Predicate<'db>>>,\n    ) {\n        let interner = self.interner;\n        let opaque_id = def_id.expect_opaque_ty();\n        // Require that the hidden type is well-formed. We have to\n        // make sure we wf-check the hidden type to fix #114728.\n        //\n        // However, we don't check that all types are well-formed.\n        // We only do so for types provided by the user or if they are\n        // \"used\", e.g. for method selection.\n        //\n        // This means we never check the wf requirements of the hidden\n        // type during MIR borrowck, causing us to infer the wrong\n        // lifetime for its member constraints which then results in\n        // unexpected region errors.\n        goals.push(Goal::new(interner, param_env, ClauseKind::WellFormed(hidden_ty.into())));\n\n        let replace_opaques_in = |clause: Clause<'db>| {\n            fold_tys(interner, clause, |ty| match ty.kind() {\n                // Replace all other mentions of the same opaque type with the hidden type,\n                // as the bounds must hold on the hidden type after all.\n                TyKind::Alias(\n                    AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n                    AliasTy { def_id: def_id2, args: args2, .. },\n                ) if def_id == def_id2 && args == args2 => hidden_ty,\n                _ => ty,\n            })\n        };\n\n        let item_bounds = opaque_id.predicates(interner.db);\n        for predicate in item_bounds.iter_instantiated_copied(interner, args.as_slice()) {\n            let predicate = replace_opaques_in(predicate);\n\n            // Require that the predicate holds for the concrete type.\n            debug!(?predicate);\n            goals.push(Goal::new(interner, param_env, predicate));\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn fetch_eligible_assoc_item(\n        &self,\n        _goal_trait_ref: rustc_type_ir::TraitRef<Self::Interner>,\n        trait_assoc_def_id: SolverDefId,\n .find_map(|(impl_assoc_name, impl_assoc_id)| {\n                        if let AssocItemId::ConstId(impl_assoc_id) = *impl_assoc_id\n                            && impl_assoc_name == trait_assoc_name\n                        {\n                            Some(impl_assoc_id)\n                        } else {\n                            None\n                        }\n                    })\n                    .map(SolverDefId::ConstId)\n            }\n            _ => panic!(\"Unexpected SolverDefId\"),\n        };\n        Ok(id)\n    }\n\n    fn is_transmutable(\n }\n\n    fn evaluate_const(\n        &self,\n        _param_env: ParamEnv<'db>,\n        uv: rustc_type_ir::UnevaluatedConst<Self::Interner>,\n    ) -> Option<<Self::Interner as rustc_type_ir::Interner>::Const> {\n        match uv.def.0 {\n            GeneralConstId::ConstId(c) => {\n                let subst = uv.args;\n                let ec = self.cx().db.const_eval(c, subst, None).ok()?;\n                Some(ec)\n            }\n            GeneralConstId::StaticId(c) => {\n                let ec = self.cx().db.const_eval_static(c).ok()?;\n                Some(ec)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn compute_goal_fast_path(\n        &self,\n        goal: rustc_type_ir::solve::Goal<\n            Self::Interner,\n            <Self::Interner as rustc_type_ir::Interner>::Predicate,\n        >,\n        _span: <Self::Interner as rustc_type_ir::Interner>::Span,\n    ) -> Option<Certainty> {\n        if let Some(trait_pred) = goal.predicate.as_trait_clause() {\n            if self.shallow_resolve(trait_pred.self_ty().skip_binder()).is_ty_var()\n                // We don't do this fast path when opaques are defined since we may\n                // eventually use opaques to incompletely guide inference via ty var\n                // self types.\n                // FIXME: Properly consider opaques here.\n                && self.inner.borrow_mut().opaque_types().is_empty()\n            {\n                return Some(Certainty::AMBIGUOUS);\n            }\n\n            if trait_pred.polarity() == PredicatePolarity::Positive {\n                match self.0.cx().as_trait_lang_item(trait_pred.def_id()) {\n                    Some(SolverTraitLangItem::Sized) | Some(SolverTraitLangItem::MetaSized) => {\n                        let predicate = self.resolve_vars_if_possible(goal.predicate);\n                        if sizedness_fast_path(self.cx(), predicate, goal.param_env) {\n                            return Some(Certainty::Yes);\n                        }\n                    }\n                    Some(SolverTraitLangItem::Copy | SolverTraitLangItem::Clone) => {\n                        let self_ty =\n                            self.resolve_vars_if_possible(trait_pred.self_ty().skip_binder());\n                        // Unlike `Sized` traits, which always prefer the built-in impl,\n                        // `Copy`/`Clone` may be shadowed by a param-env candidate which\n                        // could force a lifetime error or guide inference. While that's\n                        // not generally desirable, it is observable, so for now let's\n                        // ignore this fast path for types that have regions or infer.\n                        if !self_ty\n                            .has_type_flags(TypeFlags::HAS_FREE_REGIONS | TypeFlags::HAS_INFER)\n                            && self_ty.is_trivially_pure_clone_copy()\n                        {\n                            return Some(Certainty::Yes);\n                        }\n                    }\n                    _ => {}\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        let pred = goal.predicate.kind();\n        match pred.no_bound_vars()? {\n            PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::RegionOutlives(_outlives)) => Some(Certainty::Yes),\n            PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::TypeOutlives(_outlives)) => Some(Certainty::Yes),\n            PredicateKind::Subtype(SubtypePredicate { a, b, .. })\n            | PredicateKind::Coerce(CoercePredicate { a, b }) => {\n                if self.shallow_resolve(a).is_ty_var() && self.shallow_resolve(b).is_ty_var() {\n                    // FIXME: We also need to register a subtype relation between these vars\n                    // when those are added, and if they aren't in the same sub root then\n                    // we should mark this goal as `has_changed`.\n                    Some(Certainty::AMBIGUOUS)\n                } else {\n                    None\n                }\n            }\n            PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::ConstArgHasType(ct, _)) => {\n                if self.shallow_resolve_const(ct).is_ct_infer() {\n                    Some(Certainty::AMBIGUOUS)\n                } else {\n                    None\n                }\n            }\n            PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::WellFormed(arg)) => {\n                if arg.is_trivially_wf(self.interner) {\n                    Some(Certainty::Yes)\n                } else if arg.is_infer() {\n                    Some(Certainty::AMBIGUOUS)\n                } else {\n                    None\n                }\n            }\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":13,"oldLines":7,"newStart":13,"newLines":7,"lines":[" "," use crate::next_solver::{","     AliasTy, CanonicalVarKind, Clause, ClauseKind, CoercePredicate, GenericArgs, ImplIdWrapper,","-    ParamEnv, Predicate, PredicateKind, SubtypePredicate, Ty, TyKind, fold::fold_tys,","+    ParamEnv, Predicate, PredicateKind, SubtypeRelation, Ty, TyKind, fold::fold_tys,","     util::sizedness_fast_path,"," };"," "]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}
